The Hatim: Its Legal Status and Effect on Tawaf
The passage defines the Hatim and states the ruling that tawaf must be performed outside it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on circumambulating inside the Hatim and explain why it is invalid.

Core Idea
The Hatim is part of the Ka'ba; tawaf inside it is invalid.

The Hatim (also called al-Hijr or the Enclosure of Isma'il) is a semicircular wall north of the Ka'ba. Scholars unanimously agree that it is part of the original structure of the House. Therefore, tawaf must be performed outside it; any part of tawaf that goes inside the Hatim does not count.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hatim
Locate the Hatim on the north side of the Ka'ba; it is the area enclosed by a low wall where the waterspout is.
2
Understand its legal status
The text states that it is 'from the House' – i.e., part of the Ka'ba. Thus, circumambulation must include its area by going around it, not through it.
3
Apply the ruling
If a person walks inside the Hatim during tawaf, that circuit is invalid because part of the Ka'ba was not circumambulated. The pilgrim must ensure they stay outside.
4
Note the additional virtue
The hadith mentions that supplication against an oppressor inside the Hatim will be answered, but this does not change the requirement for tawaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
* قوله: (ويجعلُ طوافه من وراء الحطيم)؛ لأنه من البيت. وهو موضع يصب فيه الميزاب، سُمِّي به ؛ لأنه حطم من البيت، أي كُسِر.
ويُسمَّى: الحجرُ أيضاً؛ لأنه حجر من البيت، أي منع.
ويسمى: حظيرة إسماعيل.
وفي الحديث : مَن دعا على مَن ظَلَمَه فيه : حَطَمَه الله» (۱).
*
قوله: (ويَرمُلُ في الأشواط الثلاث الأول).
الرمل: بفتحتين: سرعة المشي، مع تقارب الخُطى، وهز الكتفين، مع الاضطباع، وهو السنة.
قال في «الهداية»(۲): كان سببه إظهار الجلد للمشركين حين قالوا: أضنتهم حُمَّى يَثرب، ثم بقي الحكم بعد زوال السبب، كالإخفاء في صلاة الظهر والعصر، كان لتشويش الكفرة، وأذاهم للمسلمين عند قراءتهم
القرآن في صلاتهم.
قوله: (ويمشي فيما بقي على هيئته أي على السكينة والوقار على
رسله.
* His saying: (And he makes his circumambulation from behind the Hatim) because it is part of the House. It is the place where the waterspout pours, called thus because it was broken off from the House, i.e., shattered. It is also called al-Hijr because it was separated from the House, i.e., prevented. It is also called the Enclosure of Isma'il. There is a hadith: 'Whoever supplicates against one who wronged him within it, Allah will break him.' * His saying: (And he does raml in the first three circuits). Raml (with two fatha marks) is quick walking with short steps and shaking of the shoulders, along with idtiba', and it is Sunnah. He said in al-Hidayah: Its reason was to show strength to the polytheists when they said, 'The fever of Yathrib has weakened them,' then the ruling remained after the reason ceased, similar to the lowering of voice in Zuhr and Asr prayers, which was to disturb the disbelievers and their harming the Muslims when they recited the Quran in their prayer. His saying: (And he walks in the remaining in his normal manner) i.e., with calmness and dignity, at his ease.
Source pages p. 343

Commentary
The commentator continues explaining the rulings of tawaf. Firstly, the pilgrim must perform tawaf outside the Hatim (al-Hijr, also known as the enclosure of Isma'il) because it is considered part of the Ka'ba. The names are explained: it was broken off (hattima) from the House, and thus the area is included in the circumambulation perimeter. A hadith is cited about the virtue of supplication there. Secondly, the sunnah of raml is described: quick but short steps with shoulder movement, accompanied by idtiba'. The commentator from al-Hidayah mentions the historical reason: the Prophet ﷺ and his Companions showed vigorous walking to disprove the polytheists' claim that the Muslims were weakened by fever. The ruling remained after the reason lest the sunnah be abandoned, just as the recitation in Zuhr and Asr prayers is kept quiet because originally it disturbed the disbelievers. Thirdly, in the remaining four circuits, the pilgrim walks calmly with dignity.

Key Terms
حطيم (hatim): The semicircular wall area north of the Ka'ba, considered part of the House; the pilgrim must circumambulate outside it.
حجر (hijr): Another name for the Hatim, meaning 'separated' or 'prevented'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling regarding circumambulation through the Hatim?
A) It is permissible but makruh.
B) It is invalid; the circuit must be repeated.
C) It is valid if done unknowingly.
D) It is obligatory to enter the Hatim.

Key Takeaway
The Hatim is part of the Ka'ba; tawaf must be performed outside it, and any circuit passing through it is invalid.

Raml: Its Ruling, Reason, and Application
The passage defines raml, explains its historical reason, and states that it is sunnah in the first three circuits.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of raml, explain its original reason, and apply the principle of continuity of a sunnah after the reason ceases.

Core Idea
Raml is a sunnah mu'akkadah for men in the first three circuits; its original reason ceased but the ruling remains.

Raml is a brisk, energetic walk with short steps and shoulder movement, performed by men during the first three circuits of tawaf while baring the right shoulder (idtiba'). The Prophet ﷺ and his Companions did raml to show the polytheists that the Muslims were strong and not weakened by the fever of Yathrib. Although the threat is long gone, the sunnah of raml has been preserved.

Guided Path
1
Define raml and idtiba'
Raml is quick walking with short steps and shoulder movement; idtiba' means baring the right shoulder. Both are done together in the first three circuits.
2
Identify the ruling
Raml is sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah) for men. Women do not perform raml or idtiba'.
3
Understand the historical reason (sabab)
The original reason was to demonstrate physical strength to the polytheists who claimed the Muslims were weak. The Prophet ﷺ and his Companions performed raml to disprove this.
4
Apply the principle of continuity
The ruling of raml remained despite the reason ceasing, similar to the lowering of voice in Zuhr and Asr prayers. This preserves an established sunnah.
The analogy is a qiyas.
5
Distinguish between circuits
Raml is only for the first three circuits; the remaining four circuits are performed with calm and dignity, with normal walking.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
* قوله: (ويجعلُ طوافه من وراء الحطيم)؛ لأنه من البيت. وهو موضع يصب فيه الميزاب، سُمِّي به ؛ لأنه حطم من البيت، أي كُسِر.
ويُسمَّى: الحجرُ أيضاً؛ لأنه حجر من البيت، أي منع.
ويسمى: حظيرة إسماعيل.

الرمل: بفتحتين: سرعة المشي، مع تقارب الخُطى، وهز الكتفين، مع الاضطباع، وهو السنة.

* His saying: (And he makes his circumambulation from behind the Hatim) because it is part of the House. It is the place where the waterspout pours, called thus because it was broken off from the House, i.e., shattered. It is also called al-Hijr because it was separated from the House, i.e., prevented. It is also called the Enclosure of Isma'il. There is a hadith: 'Whoever supplicates against one who wronged him within it, Allah will break him.' * His saying: (And he does raml in the first three circuits). Raml (with two fatha marks) is quick walking with short steps and shaking of the shoulders, along with idtiba', and it is Sunnah. He said in al-Hidayah: Its reason was to show strength to the polytheists when they said, 'The fever of Yathrib has weakened them,' then the ruling remained after the reason ceased, similar to the lowering of voice in Zuhr and Asr prayers, which was to disturb the disbelievers and their harming the Muslims when they recited the Quran in their prayer. His saying: (And he walks in the remaining in his normal manner) i.e., with calmness and dignity, at his ease.
Source pages p. 343

Commentary
The commentator continues explaining the rulings of tawaf. Firstly, the pilgrim must perform tawaf outside the Hatim (al-Hijr, also known as the enclosure of Isma'il) because it is considered part of the Ka'ba. The names are explained: it was broken off (hattima) from the House, and thus the area is included in the circumambulation perimeter. A hadith is cited about the virtue of supplication there. Secondly, the sunnah of raml is described: quick but short steps with shoulder movement, accompanied by idtiba'. The commentator from al-Hidayah mentions the historical reason: the Prophet ﷺ and his Companions showed vigorous walking to disprove the polytheists' claim that the Muslims were weakened by fever. The ruling remained after the reason lest the sunnah be abandoned, just as the recitation in Zuhr and Asr prayers is kept quiet because originally it disturbed the disbelievers. Thirdly, in the remaining four circuits, the pilgrim walks calmly with dignity.

Key Terms
رمل (raml): Quick walking with short steps and shoulder movement, performed in the first three circuits of tawaf by men.
اضطباع (idtiba'): Baring the right shoulder by placing the upper garment under the right armpit and over the left shoulder, done during raml.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because the polytheists still exist today.

C) To preserve the sunnah and avoid abandonment of an established practice.
D) Because the hadith explicitly commands it for all times.

Key Takeaway
Raml is a sunnah mu'akkadah for men in the first three circuits of tawaf; its historical reason ceased, but the sunnah continues.

Tawaf behind al-Hatim and Ramal in First Three Circuits
Commentary on two specific rulings of tawaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing tawaf behind al-Hatim and explain the sunnah of ramal in the first three circuits of tawaf al-qudum.

Core Idea
Tawaf must be outside al-Hatim; ramal is a sunnah mu'akkadah for men in the first three circuits.

In this passage from al-Jawharah al-Nayrah, the commentator clarifies two key rulings of tawaf: the requirement to circumambulate behind al-Hatim because it is part of the Kaaba, and the sunnah of ramal (brisk walking with shoulder movements) in the first three circuits. Understanding these rulings ensures the validity and optimal completion of tawaf, a central pillar of Hajj and Umrah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
Locate the two separate but related rulings: 1) tawaf must be performed from behind al-Hatim, 2) ramal is performed in the first three circuits.
The passage begins each ruling with 'يَجْعَلُ' and 'يَرْمُلُ'.
2
Understand the rationale for al-Hatim
The commentator explains that al-Hatim is part of the original structure of the Kaaba; thus tawaf must encompass it, not cut through.
The name 'Hatim' derives from 'broken off'; also called al-Hijr (prevented) and enclosure of Isma'il.
3
Analyze the ruling on ramal
Define ramal: rapid walking with short steps, swaying shoulders, accompanied by idtiba'. Note it is sunnah, not wajib.
Text explicitly says 'وهو السنة' (it is the sunnah).
4
Trace the reason and continuity
The commentator quotes al-Hidayah: the original reason was to show strength to polytheists, but the ruling remains as a confirmed sunnah, analogous to lowering voice in zuhr/asr.
This is an example of a ruling persisting after the 'illah (reason) has ceased.
5
Identify the normal pace
After the first three circuits, the pilgrim returns to normal walking with calmness and dignity.
This is the default state for the remaining circuits.

He should make his tawaf from behind al-Hatim. He should perform ramal in the first three circuits and walk in the remaining in his normal manner. * His statement: “He should make his tawaf from behind al-Hatim” because it is part of the House. It is the place where the spout pours. It was named thus because it was broken off from the House, i.e., broken. It is also called al-Hijr because it was prevented from the House, i.e., prevented. It is also called the enclosure of Isma’il. In the hadith: “Whoever supplicates against one who wronged him in it, Allah will break him.” * His statement: “He should perform ramal in the first three circuits.” Ramal (with two fatha) is rapid walking with close steps and moving the shoulders along with idtiba’, and it is sunnah. He said in al-Hidayah: Its reason was to show strength to the polytheists when they said, “The fever of Yathrib has weakened them,” then the ruling remained after the cause ceased, like lowering the voice in zuhr and asr prayers, which was because of the disturbance of the disbelievers and their harm to the Muslims when they recited the Quran in their prayer. His statement: “He should walk in the remaining in his normal manner” i.e., with calmness and dignity in his gait.
Source pages p. 343

Commentary
This passage is a commentary ruling on two aspects of tawaf: where to perform it and how to walk. First, the pilgrim must perform tawaf from behind al-Hatim (also called al-Hijr or the enclosure of Isma’il) because it is part of the original Kaaba structure. The commentator explains that it was broken off and remains part of the House. A hadith warns against oppression within it. Second, the pilgrim should perform ramal—swift walking with close steps and shoulder movements, along with idtiba’ (exposing the right shoulder)—in the first three circuits of the first tawaf upon arrival (tawaf al-qudum). This is sunnah. The commentator quotes al-Hidayah explaining that the original reason was to show physical strength to the polytheists who claimed Muslims were weakened by fever. Even though the cause ended, the practice remains, just as lowering the voice in zuhr and asr prayers remained after the initial cause of avoiding disturbance from disbelievers. In the remaining circuits, the pilgrim returns to normal walking with calmness and dignity. The ruling is based on prophetic practice and rational reasoning (istiḥsān), classifying it as sunnah mu'akkadah.

Key Terms
الحطيم (al-Hatim): The semi-circular wall adjacent to the Kaaba, considered part of the original structure.
الرمل (ar-ramal): Rapid walking with short steps and shoulder shaking, accompanied by idtiba'.
الاضطباع (al-idtiba'): Drawing the upper garment under the right armpit and exposing the right shoulder.

Istilam of the Black Stone and Yemeni Corner
Ruling on touching the Black Stone and Yemeni Corner during tawaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on istilam of the Black Stone and Yemeni Corner, and explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement regarding the Yemeni Corner.

Core Idea
Touching the Black Stone is sunnah; the Yemeni Corner is mustahabb in the authoritative view, though Muhammad considers it sunnah.

In the rituals of tawaf, the Prophet ﷺ consistently touched the Black Stone and the Yemeni Corner. The Hanafi school holds that touching the Black Stone is a sunnah at each circuit, while the Yemeni Corner elicits a difference of opinion: the dominant position (zahir al-riwayah) considers it mustahabb, but Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani regards it as sunnah. This lesson unpacks the ruling, the evidence, and the practical consequence of the dispute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its primary ruling
Determine what the pilgrim does (istilam of the Black Stone) and the ruling level (sunnah). Note the condition: 'if able' (in istata'a).
2
Distinguish the two corners
Compare the Black Stone (al-Hajar al-Aswad) and the Yemeni Corner (al-Rukn al-Yamani). The first is sunnah, the second is mustahabb in the apparent riwayah.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Note that Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani holds the Yemeni Corner as sunnah. This is a legitimate difference within the school.
4
Evaluate the mufta bihi
The text indicates 'fi zahir al-riwayah' — the relied-upon position for fatwa is that it is mustahabb. Understand how the school's authority hierarchy works.
5
Apply the qiyas with prayer
The text analogizes each circuit (shaut) to a rak'ah in prayer, with istilam of the Stone analogous to takbirat al-ihram. Recognize how this qiyas jaliy reinforces the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويستلمُ الحَجَرَ كلَّما مرَّ به إن استطاع، والرَّمَل من الحَجَر إلى الحَجَر : هو المنقول من رَمَل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم (۱) فإن زَحَمَه الناسُ في الرَّمَل قام فإذا وجد مسلكاً: رَمَل، ولا يطوف بدون الرمل في تلك الثلاثة ؛ لأنه لا بَدَلَ له، فيقف حتى يقيمه على وجه السنة، بخلاف الاستلام؛ لأن الاستقبال بدله.
قوله: (ويستلم الحجر الأسود كلَّما مرَّ به إن استطاع)؛ لأن أشواط الطواف كركعات الصلاة، فكما يفتتح كل ركعة بالتكبير: يفتتح كل شوط باستلام الحجر.
وإن لم يستطع الاستلام: استقبل، وكبر وهلل.
ويستلم الركن اليماني، وهو مستحب، في ظاهر الرواية.
وعن محمد : سنة
ولا يستلم غيرهما من الأركان؛ لأن النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام كان يستلم هذين الركنين وهما اليماني وركن الحجر الأسود (۳).
ولا يستلم غيرهما؛ لأنهما ليسا على قواعد إبراهيم عليه السلام، والقواعد: هنَّ أساس البيت.
He should touch the Stone every time he passes by if he is able. The ramal from the Stone to the Stone is what is transmitted from the ramal of the Messenger of Allah (saw). If people crowd him during ramal, he stands; then if he finds an opening, he performs ramal. He should not perform tawaf without ramal in those three circuits because it has no substitute; he stands until he performs it in the manner of sunnah, unlike istilam, because facing is its substitute. His statement: “He should touch the Black Stone every time he passes by if he is able” because the circuits of tawaf are like the rak’ahs of prayer. Just as one opens every rak’ah with takbir, one opens every circuit with istilam of the Stone. If he cannot touch, he faces it, says takbir and tahlil. He should touch the Yemeni Corner; it is mustahabb in the apparent riwayah. From Muhammad it is sunnah. He should not touch other corners because the Prophet (saw) used to touch these two corners: the Yemeni and the Black Stone corner. He should not touch others because they are not on the foundations of Ibrahim (as); the foundations are the base of the House.
Source pages p. 344

Commentary
This passage discusses the actions of istilam (touching) during tawaf. It first reiterates the ruling of ramal, emphasizing that if one cannot perform ramal due to crowding, he stands and waits for an opening; ramal has no substitute, unlike istilam where facing and takbir suffice. Then it states that the pilgrim should touch the Black Stone at the beginning of each circuit if possible, analogizing circuits to prayer rak’ahs where each begins with takbir. If touching is impossible, one faces the Stone and says takbir and tahlil. Next, the commentary presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the Yemeni Corner (al-Rukn al-Yamani): according to the apparent riwayah (zahir al-riwayah), touching it is mustahabb (recommended), whereas Imam Muhammad considers it sunnah. The preferred position (mufta bihi) is that it is mustahabb. Finally, it prohibits touching any other corners, as the Prophet only touched these two, and other corners are not on the foundations of Ibrahim. The ruling is supported by hadith and qiyas.

Key Terms
الاستلام (al-istilam): Touching or kissing the Black Stone or Yemeni Corner as an act of veneration.
الركن اليماني (ar-ruknu al-yamani): The corner of the Kaaba facing Yemen, located before the Black Stone.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The well-known transmitted rulings from Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad in the six books.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Fard
D) Makruh

Key Takeaway
Touching the Black Stone is a sunnah at each circuit; touching the Yemeni Corner is mustahabb (the mufta bihi view), though Imam Muhammad considers it sunnah — the difference is in the level of recommendation, not obligation.

Rulings of Istilam, Maqam Ibrahim, and the Two Rak'ahs After Tawaf
Commentary on post-Tawaf rites

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on istilam, Maqam Ibrahim, and the two rak'ahs after Tawaf, and identify the evidence for the wajib status of the two rak'ahs.

Core Idea
The two rak'ahs after Tawaf are wajib in the Hanafi school; omission requires a dam.

This passage from Al-Jawharah al-Nayirah explains the actions immediately after completing Tawaf: concluding with istilam, then proceeding to Maqam Ibrahim to pray two rak'ahs. It emphasizes that kissing the Yemeni corner is not sunnah, and that the two rak'ahs are wajib, with a blood sacrifice due if omitted.

Guided Path
1
Identify the post-Tawaf actions
List the three actions: concluding Tawaf with istilam, approaching Maqam Ibrahim, and praying two rak'ahs.
2
Determine the hukm level for istilam and Yemeni corner
Istilam is sunnah; kissing the Yemeni corner is not sunnah. Differentiate between Black Stone and Yemeni corner.
3
Determine the hukm level for the two rak'ahs
The text explicitly says 'وهما واجبتان عندنا' – they are wajib. If omitted, a dam is required.
4
Analyze the evidence for the wajib status
The evidence is Quran 2:125 (imperative) and a hadith about reward. The Hanafi usul principle: al-amr yufidu al-wujub.
5
Note the practical rulings
The rak'ahs can be prayed anywhere in the mosque, or even outside Mecca if necessary, but must be at a permissible time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويختم الطواف بالاستلام .
ثم يأتي مقام إبراهيم،
- ولا يُسن تقبيلُ الركن اليماني ؛ لأن النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام استلمه، ولم يُقبله.
قوله : (ويختم الطواف بالاستلام) ، يعني استلام الحجر الأسود. * قوله : (ثم يأتي المقام، يعني مقامَ إبراهيم، وهو ما ظهر فيه أثر قدميه حين كان يقوم عليه حين نزوله وركوبه حين يأتي إلى زيارة هاجر وولده إسماعيل.
فيصلي * عنده ركعتين، أو حيثما تيسر من المسجد .
والمقام بفتح الميم موضع القيام، وبضمها: موضع الإقامة. * قوله: (فيصلي عنده ركعتين) : أي عند المقام، (أو حيثما تيسر من المسجد).
وهما واجبتان عندنا، فإن تركهما ذكر في بعض المناسك: أن عليه دماً.
وإن صلاهما في غير المسجد : أو في غير مكة: جاز؛ لأنه روي أن عمر رضي الله عنه نسيهما، وصلاهما بذي طوى. ذكره «في الكرخي». وقد ورد أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم لما فرغ من الطواف: صلى في المقام ركعتين، وتلا قوله تعالى: ﴿وَاتَّخِذُوا مِن مَّقَامِ إِبْرَاهِيمَ مُصَلَّى ... البقرة / ١٢٥ . وقال عليه الصلاة والسلام: مَن صلى خلف المقام ركعتين: غفر الله له ما تقدم من ذنبه وما تأخر، وحُشر يوم القيامة من الآمنين». كذا في كتاب «الشفا».
والمستحب أن يقرأ فيهما: ﴿قُلْ يَتَأَيُّهَا الْكَفِرُونَ ، و: قُلْ هُوَ الله أحد).
فإذا فرغ: يدعو لنفسه ولوالديه وللمسلمين.
ولا يصليهما إلا في وقت مباح
He concludes the Tawaf with istilam. Then he comes to Maqam Ibrahim. And it is not sunnah to kiss the Yemeni corner, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) touched it and did not kiss it. His statement: 'and he concludes the Tawaf with istilam' means touching the Black Stone. His statement: 'then he comes to the Maqam' means Maqam Ibrahim, which is the place where the trace of his feet appeared when he stood on it during his descent and ascent when he came to visit Hagar and her son Ishmael. He prays by it two rak'ahs, or wherever is easy in the mosque. 'Al-Maqam' with fath of the meem is the place of standing; with damm it is the place of residence. His statement: 'he prays by it two rak'ahs' means at the Maqam, 'or wherever is easy in the mosque'. These two are obligatory in our school; if one leaves them, it is mentioned in some manasik that he must offer a blood sacrifice. If he prays them outside the mosque or outside Mecca, it is permissible, because it is narrated that Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) forgot them and prayed them at Dhi Tuwa. This was mentioned in al-Karkhi. It has been narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him), when he finished the Tawaf, prayed two rak'ahs at the Maqam and recited the verse: 'And take the Maqam of Ibrahim as a place of prayer' (al-Baqarah 2:125). And he (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever prays two rak'ahs behind the Maqam, Allah will forgive him his previous and later sins, and he will be gathered on the Day of Resurrection among the secure.' This is in the book 'al-Shifa'. It is recommended to recite in them 'Say, O disbelievers' and 'Say, He is Allah, the One'. When he finishes, he supplicates for himself, his parents, and the Muslims. He should not pray them except in a permissible time.
Source pages p. 345

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the Mukhtasar al-Quduri, explaining the actions immediately after completing the seven circuits of Tawaf. The author begins by stating that the Tawaf is concluded with 'istilam', i.e. touching or kissing the Black Stone. He then notes that it is not sunnah to kiss the Yemeni corner (al-Rukn al-Yamani), because the Prophet (peace be upon him) only touched it and did not kiss it. This is the established Hanafi position; though some narrations mention kissing, they are considered weak. Next, the pilgrim proceeds to Maqam Ibrahim, the stone that bears the footprint of Prophet Ibrahim (peace be upon him). The author mentions the linguistic difference: 'maqam' (with fath) means place of standing, while 'muqam' (with damm) means place of residence. The pilgrim then prays two rak'ahs near the Maqam, or anywhere in the mosque if it is crowded. The two rak'ahs are wajib (obligatory) in the Hanafi school, and if omitted, a sacrificial blood (dam) is required. However, if one prays them outside the mosque or even outside Mecca, it is still valid, as evidenced by the action of Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) who prayed them at Dhi Tuwa. The proof for praying at the Maqam includes the Quranic verse 'And take the Maqam of Ibrahim as a place of prayer' (2:125) and a hadith promising great reward for the two rak'ahs behind the Maqam. The recommended surahs to recite are Surah al-Kafirun and Surah al-Ikhlas. After the prayer, one should supplicate for oneself, parents, and all Muslims. Finally, the prayer must be performed at a permissible time (i.e., not during prohibited times such as sunrise, noon, and sunset).

Key Terms
الاستلام (al-istilam): Touching or kissing the Black Stone during Tawaf.
مقام إبراهيم (Maqam Ibrahim): A stone near the Kaaba containing the footprint of Prophet Ibrahim; the place where he stood while building the Kaaba.
الركن اليماني (al-Rukn al-Yamani): The Yemeni corner of the Kaaba, between the Black Stone and the door of the Kaaba.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling (hukm) of the two rak'ahs after Tawaf in the Hanafi school?
A) Sunnah mu'akkadah
B) Wajib, and if omitted a dam is required
C) Mubah (permissible)
D) Fard

Key Takeaway
The two rak'ahs after Tawaf are wajib in the Hanafi school, and if omitted, a dam is required; the prayer may be performed even outside the mosque if needed.

The Two Rak'ahs After Tawaf Are Wajib
Ruling on post-tawaf prayer with proofs and compensation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the two rak'ahs after tawaf, cite the primary evidence from Quran and Sunnah, and explain the distinction between wajib and fard in this context.

Core Idea
The two rak'ahs after tawaf are wajib—omission requires a dam, but the act itself remains valid.

This passage from the commentary on al-Quduri establishes a key ruling in Hajj rituals. The author explains that the two rak'ahs after tawaf are wajib, supported by the Quranic verse 'And take from the station of Ibrahim a place of prayer' and a hadith promising forgiveness. Understanding this ruling is essential for every pilgrim, as it distinguishes between wajib and fard and clarifies the consequence of omission.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is the two rak'ahs performed after completing tawaf. The ruling is wajib, not fard.
Wajib means omission requires compensation (dam), but the tawaf itself remains valid.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The Quranic verse (2:125) commands 'Wa ittakhidhu min maqami Ibrahima musalla' – take the station of Ibrahim as a place of prayer.
The imperative form indicates obligation per Hanafi usul.
3
Understand the usul principle
Hanafi usul holds that al-amr yufidu al-wujub – a command indicates obligation unless there is a contextual indicator to the contrary.
The verse's thubut is qat'i (Quran), but its dalala is zanni (derived from imperative), making the ruling wajib rather than fard.
4
Note secondary evidences
A hadith promises forgiveness for praying these two rak'ahs behind the Maqam, and the practice of 'Umar (praying them outside Mecca) shows their place is not restricted.
These reinforce the obligation and clarify flexibility in location.
5
Distinguish wajib from fard
A missing wajib does not invalidate the act; it requires compensation (dam). A missing fard invalidates the act entirely.
Thus, if one omits the two rak'ahs, the tawaf is valid but a dam is owed.

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn regarding the two rak'ahs after circumambulation (tawaf). The author explains the ruling of these two rak'ahs, which are wajib (obligatory) according to the Hanafi school, not fard. The evidence includes the Quranic verse commanding to take Maqam Ibrahim as a prayer place and the hadith of the Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wa sallam) promising great reward. The text also clarifies that if one omits them, a dam (sacrificial animal) is owed, as mentioned in some manasik works. It is permissible to pray them outside the mosque or even outside Mecca, as demonstrated by 'Umar's practice. The recommended recitation is Surah al-Kafirun and Surah al-Ikhlas. The prayer should be performed in a permissible time (i.e., not during disliked times like after Fajr and 'Asr).

ركعتا الطواف (rak'atay al-tawaf): The two rak'ahs performed after completing any tawaf, especially after tawaf al-qudum.
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal (sheep or goat) required as compensation for leaving a wajib act in Hajj or 'Umrah.

Tawaf al-Qudum: Sunnah or Wajib?
Definition and ruling of arrival tawaf and the start of sa'i.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of tawaf al-qudum and identify who is exempt from it.

Core Idea
Tawaf al-qudum is a recommended sunnah, not obligatory; omitting it requires no compensation.

In this passage, the author clarifies the legal status of tawaf al-qudum (arrival tawaf) — a ritual performed upon entering Makka. Many pilgrims assume it is mandatory, but the Hanafi school explicitly states it is a sunnah. This lesson unpacks the ruling, the exemption for locals, and the connection to sa'i.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Locate the statement 'wa huwa sunnatun wa laysa bi wajib'. Understand that tawaf al-qudum is recommended but not required. Note that if omitted, there is no penalty.
2
Recognize the exemption for Makkans
The text says 'laysa 'ala ahli Makka tawaf al-qudum'. This includes all those living within the miqat boundaries. Ask: Why? Because they do not 'arrive' from outside.
The same exemption applies to people of the miqat itself.
3
Understand the sequence after tawaf
After performing tawaf al-qudum, the pilgrim goes to Safa to begin sa'i. The text explains that one returns to the Black Stone and performs istilam because sa'i is opened in the same way tawaf is opened.
If there is no sa'i after the tawaf (e.g., tawaf al-ifada), one does not return to the stone.
4
Note the adab of exiting to Safa
It is preferred to exit through the door of Safa (Bab Bani Makhzum), but this is not a sunnah; any door is acceptable. Ascending Safa to see the Kaaba is recommended for istiqbal.
The emphasis is on the purpose of facing the Kaaba, not the specific route.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذا الطواف طواف القدوم، وهو سنة وليس بواجب . وليس على أهل مكة طواف القدوم. ثم يخرج إلى الصفا، فيصعد عليه، ثم يعود إلى الحَجَرِ، فيستلمه؛ لأن الطواف لما كان يفتتح بالاستلام : فكذلك السعي يفتتح به. بخلاف ما إذا لم يكن بعد الطواف سعي: فإنه لا يعود إلى الحجر فيه. قوله: (وهذا الطواف طوافُ القُدوم)، ويسمى: طواف التحية، وطواف اللقاء، وطواف أول عهد بالبيت. قوله: (وهو سُنَّةٌ، وليس بواجب، حتى لو تركه لم يكن عليه شيء. كذا في «الخجندي». قوله: (وليس على أهل مكة طواف القدوم)؛ لانعدام القدوم منهم. وكذا من كان من أهل المواقيت ومن دونها إلى مكة؛ لأنهم في حكم أهل مكة. قوله: (ثم يخرج إلى الصفا والأفضل أن يخرج من باب الصفا، وهو باب بني مخزوم، وليس ذلك سنة عندنا ولو خرج من غيره: جاز. قوله: (فيصعد عليه) : أي يصعد بحيث يرى البيت؛ لأن الاستقبال هو المقصود بالصعود.
And this tawaf is tawaf al-qudum (arrival tawaf), and it is sunnah and not wajib. There is no tawaf al-qudum for the people of Makka. Then he goes out to Safa, ascends upon it, then returns to the Black Stone and kisses/ touches it because just as tawaf is opened with istilam, so sa'i is opened with it. Unlike when there is no sa'i after tawaf, then he does not return to the stone in it. His saying: (And this tawaf is tawaf al-qudum) and it is called tawaf al-tahiyyah, tawaf al-liqa', and tawaf awwal 'ahd bil-bayt. His saying: (It is sunnah and not wajib, so if he leaves it, there is nothing upon him. As in al-Khujandi. His saying: (There is no tawaf al-qudum for the people of Makka) because there is no arrival from them. Similarly, whoever is from the people of the miqats and those within [the miqat] to Makka; they are in the ruling of the people of Makka. His saying: (Then he goes out to Safa and it is best to go out through the door of Safa, which is the door of Banu Makhzum, but that is not sunnah according to us; if he goes out from another [door], it is permissible. His saying: (He ascends upon it) i.e., he ascends such that he sees the House (Kaaba), because facing it (istiqbal) is the purpose of ascending.
Source pages p. 347

Commentary
This passage explains tawaf al-qudum (the arrival tawaf), which is the first tawaf performed by someone entering Makka for Hajj or 'Umrah. According to the Hanafi school, it is sunnah (recommended), not wajib (obligatory). Thus, if one omits it, there is no penalty. The people of Makka and those who live within the miqat boundaries are exempt because they do not 'arrive' from outside. After this tawaf, the pilgrim goes to the hill of Safa to begin sa'i. The author mentions that it is preferred to exit through the door of Safa (Bab Bani Makhzum), but it is not a sunnah; any exit is permissible. Ascending Safa so that one can see the Kaaba is recommended because facing the Kaaba is the purpose. The commentary also notes that after sa'i, one returns to the Black Stone and performs istilam (touching or kissing), mirroring the opening of tawaf. However, if there is no sa'i after tawaf, one does not return to the stone.

Key Terms
طواف القدوم (tawaf al-qudum): The tawaf performed upon arrival in Makka by those coming from outside the miqat; also called tawaf al-tahiyyah.
الصفا (al-Safa): A small hill near the Kaaba from which the sa'i (walking between Safa and Marwa) begins.
السعي (sa'i): The ritual of walking seven times between Safa and Marwa, an integral part of Hajj and 'Umrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Tawaf al-qudum is a sunnah, not wajib; it is recommended for those arriving from outside Makka, and omitting it incurs no penalty.

Tawaf al-Qudum: A Sunnah, Not an Obligation
Ruling and procedure for Tawaf al-Qudum and opening Sa'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Tawaf al-Qudum and identify the recommended actions when beginning Sa'i after tawaf.

Core Idea
Tawaf al-Qudum is a stressed sunnah; omitting it incurs no penalty.

This passage from Al-Jawharah al-Nayirah clarifies the ruling of Tawaf al-Qudum, the arrival circumambulation performed by non-Makkans upon reaching Makkah. The commentator emphasizes that it is sunnah, not wajib, and details the procedure when Sa'i follows the tawaf, including returning to the Black Stone and the recommended supplications on Safa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Locate the explicit statement that Tawaf al-Qudum is sunnah, not wajib. Note that omitting it has no penalty.
The text says: 'وهو سنة وليس بواجب'.
2
Recognize the exemption for Makkans
Understand that people of Makkah and those within the miqat boundaries are exempt from Tawaf al-Qudum because they have no 'arrival'.
The commentator explains: 'لانعدام القدوم منهم'.
3
Understand the connection between tawaf and Sa'i
After tawaf, if one intends Sa'i, he should return to the Black Stone for istilam, mirroring the opening of tawaf. If no Sa'i follows, he does not return.
The text contrasts the two scenarios.
4
Review the recommended actions on Safa
Ascend Safa until the Kaaba is visible, face it, say takbir, tahlil, salawat, and make dua with raised hands.
These are sunan, not obligations.
5
Note the emphasis on dua at completion
Dua is mentioned here because it marks the completion of the tawaf, similar to the end of prayer.
The commentator cites Hasan al-Basri's list of answered dua places.

وليس على أهل مكة طواف القدوم.
ثم يخرج إلى الصفا، فيصعد عليه،
ثم يعود إلى الحَجَرِ، فيستلمه؛ لأن الطواف لما كان يفتتح بالاستلام : فكذلك السعي يفتتح به.
بخلاف ما إذا لم يكن بعد الطواف سعي: فإنه لا يعود إلى الحجر فيه.
قوله: (وهذا الطواف طوافُ القُدوم)، ويسمى: طواف التحية، وطواف اللقاء، وطواف أول عهد بالبيت.

ثم ينحط نحو المروة، ويمشي على هيئته،
قوله: (ويستقبل البيت، ويُكبر ويُهلِّل، ويصلي على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم، ويدعو الله تعالى بحاجته)، ويرفع يديه عند الدعاء نحو السماء. قوله : ويدعو الله بحاجته إنما ذكر الدعاء هنا، ولم يذكره عند استلام الحجر ؛ لأن الاستلام حالة ابتداء العبادة، وهذا: حالة ختمها، فإن ختم الطواف بالسعي والدعاء إنما يكون عند الفراغ من العبادة، لا عند ابتدائها، كما في الصلاة.

The Book of Hajj
This circumambulation is Tawaf al-Qudum, and it is sunnah, not obligatory.
Tawaf al-Qudum is not required of the people of Makkah.
Then he goes out to as-Safa and ascends upon it,
Then he returns to the Black Stone and touches it; because just as the circumambulation is opened with the touching (istilam), so too the Sa'i is opened with it.
Unlike when there is no Sa'i after the circumambulation: then he does not return to the Black Stone for it.
His saying: (This circumambulation is Tawaf al-Qudum), and it is called: Tawaf at-Tahiyyah, Tawaf al-Liqa, and Tawaf Awwal 'Ahd bil-Bayt.
His saying: (It is sunnah, not obligatory, such that if one abandons it, nothing is due from him. Thus in al-Khujandi.
His saying: (Tawaf al-Qudum is not required of the people of Makkah) because there is no coming (qudum) from them. Similarly, whoever is from the people of the miqat and those between it and Makkah; because they are in the ruling of the people of Makkah.
His saying: (Then he goes out to as-Safa and it is better that he go out from the gate of as-Safa, which is the gate of Banu Makhzum, and that is not sunnah according to us, and if he goes out from another, it is permissible. As-Safa is named because when Adam (peace be upon him) came to it, he said: 'Welcome, O Safiyy of Allah.' And his saying: (ascends upon it) means he ascends such that he sees the House; because facing it (istiqbal) is the purpose of ascending.
He faces the House, says Allahu Akbar, Tahlil, sends salawat upon the Prophet (peace be upon him), and supplicates to Allah Almighty for his need.
Then he descends towards al-Marwah, walking in his manner.
His saying: (He faces the House, says Allahu Akbar, Tahlil, sends salawat upon the Prophet, and supplicates to Allah for his need), and he raises his hands in supplication towards the sky. His saying: 'and supplicates to Allah for his need' – He mentioned supplication here, and did not mention it at the touching of the Black Stone (istilam), because the touching is the beginning of the act of worship, and this is the completion of it; for the completion of the circumambulation with Sa'i and supplication is only at the completion of the act of worship, not at its beginning, just as in prayer.
Al-Hasan al-Basri said: 'Supplication is answered in fifteen places: in the circumambulation, at the Multazam, under the Mizab, in the House, at Zamzam, on as-Safa, on al-Marwah, in the Sa'i, behind the Maqam, in 'Arafat, in Muzdalifah, in Mina, and at the three Jamarat.'
So deprived is the one who does not strive in supplication in these places.
It is recommended to recite a complete Quranic recitation (khatmah) in the circumambulation during the days of the season (Mawsim).
* His saying: (Then he descends towards al-Marwah, walking in his manner) means with tranquility and dignity, and he says in his Sa'i: 'O Lord, forgive and have mercy, and overlook what You know, indeed You are
Source pages p. 347

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the rulings of Tawaf al-Qudum (the arrival circumambulation) and the beginning of the Sa'i between Safa and Marwah. The commentator explains that Tawaf al-Qudum is a sunnah, not an obligation, and therefore no penalty is incurred by omitting it. People of Makkah and those within the miqat boundaries are exempt from this tawaf because the concept of 'arrival' (qudum) does not apply to them. The commentator then discusses the procedure: after tawaf, if one intends Sa'i, he should return to the Black Stone to touch it (istilam) as the opening for Sa'i, mirroring the opening of tawaf. If no Sa'i follows, one does not return to the stone. The commentary then details the actions on Safa: ascending until one can see the Kaaba, facing it, saying takbir, tahlil, salawat, and making dua with raised hands. The dua is emphasized because it marks the completion of the tawaf, paralleling the end of prayer. The passage also cites a tradition from Hasan al-Basri listing fifteen places where dua is particularly answered, including the tawaf and Sa'i. Finally, it mentions the recommendation to recite a complete Quranic recitation during the days of the Hajj season and the dignified walking during Sa'i, with a recommended supplication.

Key Terms
طواف القدوم (Tawaf al-Qudum): The circumambulation performed upon arrival in Makkah for Hajj or Umrah; it is a sunnah, not obligatory.
السعي (as-Sa'i): The ritual walking between Safa and Marwah, a pillar of Hajj and Umrah.
الصفا (as-Safa): A small hill near the Kaaba, the starting point of the Sa'i.
الاستلام (al-Istilam): Touching or kissing the Black Stone as an opening act of tawaf and Sa'i.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on Tawaf al-Qudum?
A) It is wajib (obligatory).
B) It is sunnah (recommended), not wajib.
C) It is fard (required).
D) It is optional with penalty for omission.

Key Takeaway
Tawaf al-Qudum is a sunnah muakkadah, and its omission requires no compensation, unlike wajib or fard acts.

The Procedure of Sa'i between Safa and Marwa
Describes the actions and duas during sa'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the actions of sa'i between Safa and Marwa, including the recommended supplications and the ruling on running between the two markers.

Core Idea
Sa'i between Safa and Marwa is a wajib rite performed in seven circuits, beginning at Safa and ending at Marwa, with supplication and running in the valley.

The ritual of sa'i (walking between Safa and Marwa) is a central component of Hajj and Umrah. In this lesson, we examine the detailed procedure as described in the Hanafi text al-Jawharah al-Nayrah, including the recommended actions upon ascending the hills, the supplications to recite, and the ruling on jogging in the valley area. Understanding these details ensures the pilgrim performs this wajib act correctly, avoiding common errors.

Guided Path
1
Identify the components of sa'i
List the main actions: facing the Kaaba, supplication, walking, running, and the seven circuits.
The text describes each action in order: ascent on Safa, supplication, descent, running, ascent on Marwa, repetition.
2
Understand the place of supplication
Supplication is emphasized after tawaf at the start of sa'i, not during tawaf, because it marks the completion of one worship and the beginning of another.
Analogy with prayer: supplication at the end of prayer is more emphasized.
3
Analyze the valley floor running
The pilgrim runs briskly (harwalah) only between the two green markers, not the entire distance. The markers indicate the historic valley.
One marker is green, the other red; they are carved from the mosque wall.
4
Count the circuits
Sa'i consists of seven circuits. Each circuit is one traversal from Safa to Marwa or vice versa. The first begins at Safa, the seventh ends at Marwa.
The text explicitly states the correct view: seven circuits starting at Safa and ending at Marwa.
5
Note the recommended duas
During walking, recite: 'Rabbi ighfir wa rham...' (Lord, forgive and have mercy...). Also, general supplications are recommended.
The text provides the specific du'a: 'Rabbi ighfir wa rham wa tajaawaz 'amma ta'lam...'

Source Text

ويستقبل البيت، ويكبر ويهلل، ويصلي على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم، ويدعو الله تعالى بحاجته . ثم ينحط نحو المروة، ويمشي على هيئته، قوله: (ويستقبل البيت، ويُكبر ويُهلِّل، ويصلي على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم، ويدعو الله تعالى بحاجته)، ويرفع يديه عند الدعاء نحو السماء. قوله : ويدعو الله بحاجته إنما ذكر الدعاء هنا، ولم يذكره عند استلام الحجر ؛ لأن الاستلام حالة ابتداء العبادة، وهذا: حالة ختمها، فإن ختم الطواف بالسعي والدعاء إنما يكون عند الفراغ من العبادة، لا عند ابتدائها، كما في الصلاة. «قال الحسن البصري: الدعاء مستجاب في خمسة عشر موضعاً: في الطواف، وعند الملتزم، وتحت الميزاب، وفي البيت، وعند زمزم، وعلى الصفا، وعلى المروة، وفي السعي، وخلف المقام، وفي عرفات، وفي المزدلفة، وفي منى، وعند الجمرات الثلاث»(۱). فمحروم من لا يجتهد في الدعاء في هذه المواضع. ويستحب أن يقرأ في أيام الموسم ختمةٌ في الطواف. * قوله : (ثم ينحط نحو المروة، ويمشي على هيئته) : أي على السكينة والوقار، ويقول في سعيه : رب اغفر وارحم ، وتجاوز عما تعلم، إنك أنت الأعز الأكرم، واهدني للتي هي أقوم، فإنك تعلم ولا أعلم. * قوله: (فإذا بلغ إلى بطن الوادي: سعى بين الميلين الأخضرين سعياً). وهما علامتان لموضع الهرولة، وهما شيئان منحوتان من جدار المسجد الحرام، لا أنهما منفصلان عن الجدار. وسماهما : أخضرين على طريق الأغلب، وإلا فأحدهما أخضر، والآخر أحمر. ولم يكن اليوم بطن وادي؛ لأنه قد كبسته السيول، فجعل هناك ميلان؛ علامةً لموضع الهرولة؛ ليعرف أنه بطن الوادي. قوله: (حتى يأتي المَرْوة) : بإسكان الياء؛ لأنه لو نصب: لأفهم أن السعي إلى أن يأتي المروة، وليس هو كذلك. * قوله : فيصعد عليها ويفعل كما فعل على الصفا)، يعني من التكبير والتهليل، والصلاة على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم، والدعاء، والرفع. * قوله: (وهذا شَوْط)، وهو الصحيح. * قوله: (فيطوف سبعة أشواط، يبتدىء بالصفا، ويختم بالمروة)؛
He faces the House, and says Allahu Akbar and la ilaha illa Allah, and sends blessings upon the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, and supplicates to Allah Almighty for his need. Then he descends towards Marwa, walking in his [usual] manner. His statement: (And he faces the House, and says Allahu Akbar, and la ilaha illa Allah, and sends blessings upon the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, and supplicates to Allah Almighty for his need), and he raises his hands in supplication towards the sky. His statement: And he supplicates to Allah for his need – he mentioned supplication here, but did not mention it at the touching of the Black Stone, because touching is a state of beginning the worship, whereas this is a state of completing it. For the completion of tawaf with sa'i and supplication occurs only at the completion of the worship, not at its beginning, as in prayer. Al-Hasan al-Basri said: 'Supplication is answered in fifteen places: during tawaf, at the Multazam, under the waterspout, inside the House, at Zamzam, on Safa, on Marwa, during sa'i, behind the Maqam, at Arafat, at Muzdalifah, at Mina, and at the three Jamarat.' So deprived is the one who does not strive in supplication in these places. And it is recommended to complete a recitation of the Quran during the days of the season in tawaf. * His statement: (Then he descends towards Marwa, and walks in his manner): i.e., with tranquility and dignity, and he says during his sa'i: 'O Lord, forgive and have mercy, and overlook what You know. Indeed, You are the Most Mighty, the Most Generous. Guide me to that which is most upright, for You know and I do not know.' * His statement: (When he reaches the valley floor, he runs between the two green markers, running). They are two markers for the place of jogging, and they are two things carved from the wall of the Sacred Mosque, not separate from the wall. He called them 'green' as a general description, otherwise one is green and the other is red. Today there is no valley floor because floods have covered it, so two markers were placed there as a sign for the place of jogging, so that it be known that it is the valley floor. His statement: (until he reaches Marwa): with sukun on the ya, because if it were in the accusative, it would give the impression that the sa'i continues until he reaches Marwa, but it is not so. * His statement: (He ascends it and does as he did on Safa), meaning takbir, tahlil, sending blessings upon the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, supplication, and raising [the hands]. * His statement: (This is one circuit), and it is correct. * His statement: (He performs seven circuits, beginning with Safa and ending with Marwa);
Source pages p. 348

Commentary
This passage describes the actions of sa'i between Safa and Marwa, which is a required (wajib) rite of Hajj and Umrah according to the Hanafi school. The text explains that when the pilgrim ascends Safa, he should face the Kaaba, recite takbir and tahlil, send blessings on the Prophet (ﷺ), and make supplication with raised hands. The commentary notes that supplication is mentioned here rather than at the touching of the Black Stone because touching is the beginning of worship, while after tawaf is a completion, analogous to prayer. A quote from Hasan al-Basri lists fifteen places where supplication is answered, emphasizing the virtue of these locations. The pilgrim then descends towards Marwa with calmness and dignity, reciting a specific supplication. When reaching the valley floor (batan al-wadi), he should run briskly (harwalah) between the two green markers, which are actually one green and one red marker carved from the mosque wall, serving as indicators of the historic valley that is now filled. Upon reaching Marwa, he repeats the same actions as on Safa, and this constitutes one circuit (shawt). The complete sa'i consists of seven circuits, starting from Safa and ending at Marwa, as affirmed by the correct view in the school.

Key Terms
سعي (sa'i): The ritual walking between Safa and Marwa seven times during Hajj or Umrah.
شوط (shawt): One complete traversal from Safa to Marwa (or vice versa) during sa'i.
هرولة (harwalah): A brisk jogging pace performed between the two green markers in the valley during sa'i.
بطن الوادي (batan al-wadi): The valley floor between Safa and Marwa where the running (harwalah) is performed.
الميل الأخضر (al-mil al-akhdar): The green marker (actually one green and one red) indicating the start and end of the area for running.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling of sa'i between Safa and Marwa in the Hanafi school?
A) It is sunnah mu'akkadah.
B) It is wajib; omission requires a sacrifice (dam).
C) It is fard; omission invalidates the Hajj.
D) It is mubah.

Key Takeaway
Sa'i between Safa and Marwa is a wajib act consisting of seven circuits, starting at Safa and ending at Marwa, with recommended supplications and jogging between the two markers in the valley.

Sa'y: Procedure and Refutation of al-Tahawi's View
Dispute over sa'y end point and markers description

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi procedure for sa'y (start at Safa, end at Marwah, seven circuits) and explain why al-Tahawi's alternative is rejected.

Core Idea
Sa'y is seven circuits from Safa to Marwah; ending at Safa would double the count, which is incorrect.

Sa'y between Safa and Marwah is a wajib rite of Hajj and Umrah. Its performance is clearly established: seven circuits starting at Safa and ending at Marwah. However, the Hanafi jurist al-Tahawi held a different view, claiming the circuits should begin and end at Safa. This lesson examines the correct procedure and the refutation of al-Tahawi's opinion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the correct procedure for sa'y
From the text, note that the pilgrim starts at Safa, performs seven circuits each ending at Marwah. The quick pace (ramal) is only in the valley between the two green markers.
The markers are carved from the Haram wall, one green and one red.
2
Understand the role of the two green markers
The markers indicate the place of ramal; they are not separate but part of the wall. The valley bottom is no longer visible due to flood debris.
This clarifies the physical location of the required running.
3
Analyze al-Tahawi's opposing view
Al-Tahawi proposed that sa'y should start and end at Safa, which would require fourteen climbs of Safa instead of seven.
His reasoning is not given in the text, but the consequence is doubling the circuits.
4
Evaluate the refutation
The commentator explicitly states that al-Tahawi's view is incorrect (ghayr sahih). The established practice (zahir al-riwayah) is the majority position.
The tarjih is clear: the mufta bihi is the majority view.
5
Derive the practical implication
The thamarah al-khilaf is the number of circuits: seven versus fourteen. This affects the validity of the ritual.
A pilgrim following al-Tahawi's view would be in error, performing more than required.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإذا بلغ إلى بطن الوادي : سعى بين الميلين الأخضرين سعياً حتى يأتي المروة، فيصعد عليها، ويفعلُ كما فَعَل على الصفا، وهذا شوطٌ. فيطوف سبعة أشواط، يبتدىء بالصفا، ويختم بالمروة. الأعز الأكرم، واهدني للتي هي أقوم، فإنك تعلم ولا أعلم. * قوله: (فإذا بلغ إلى بطن الوادي: سعى بين الميلين الأخضرين سعياً). وهما علامتان لموضع الهرولة، وهما شيئان منحوتان من جدار المسجد الحرام، لا أنهما منفصلان عن الجدار. وسماهما : أخضرين على طريق الأغلب، وإلا فأحدهما أخضر، والآخر أحمر. ولم يكن اليوم بطن وادي؛ لأنه قد كبسته السيول، فجعل هناك ميلان؛ علامةً لموضع الهرولة؛ ليعرف أنه بطن الوادي. قوله: (حتى يأتي المَرْوة) : بإسكان الياء؛ لأنه لو نصب: لأفهم أن السعي إلى أن يأتي المروة، وليس هو كذلك. * قوله : فيصعد عليها ويفعل كما فعل على الصفا)، يعني من التكبير والتهليل، والصلاة على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم، والدعاء، والرفع. * قوله: (وهذا شَوْط)، وهو الصحيح. * قوله: (فيطوف سبعة أشواط، يبتدىء بالصفا، ويختم بالمروة)؛ ثم يقيم بمكة مُحرِماً، يطوف بالبيت كلما بدا له، ويصلي لكل أسبوع ركعتين . احترازاً عن قول الطحاوي، فإنه قال: يبتدىء بالصفا، ويختم بالصفا، فيكون على قوله : أربعة عشر مرةً، وهو غير صحيح
When he reaches the bottom of the valley, he runs between the two green markers with a quick pace until he comes to al-Marwah, then ascends upon it and does as he did on al-Safa, and this is one circuit. He performs seven circuits, starting at al-Safa and ending at al-Marwah. (Commentary: The two markers are indicators for the place of quick pacing; they are two things carved from the wall of the Sacred Mosque, not separate from the wall. They are called green by way of prevalence; otherwise, one is green and the other red. Today there is no valley bottom because floods have covered it, so two markers were placed there as an indicator for the place of quick pacing to know that it is the valley bottom. The phrase 'until he comes to al-Marwah' with sukun on the ya; if it were nasb, it would imply that the sa'y continues until he reaches al-Marwah, which is not the case. He ascends upon it and does as he did on al-Safa, meaning takbir, tahlil, salawat upon the Prophet, supplication, and raising hands. This is one circuit, and that is correct. He performs seven circuits, starting at al-Safa and ending at al-Marwah; then he stays in Makkah as a muhrim, circumambulating the House whenever he wishes, and praying two rak'ahs for each seven circuits. (Commentary: This is as a caution against the statement of al-Tahawi, for he said: one starts at al-Safa and ends at al-Safa, so according to him it would be fourteen times, and that is incorrect.)
Source pages p. 349

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the manner of sa'y between Safa and Marwah. The text first states the ruling: when the pilgrim reaches the bottom of the valley (batan al-wadi), he should run quickly between the two green markers until he reaches al-Marwah, climb it, and do as on Safa. This completes one shawt (circuit). Seven circuits are performed, starting at Safa and ending at Marwah. The commentary explains that the two green markers are carved from the wall of the Haram, not separate. They are called 'green' commonly, but one is actually green and the other red. The valley bottom is now covered by floods, so markers indicate the place. The phrase 'hatta ya'tiya al-marwah' is with sukun to show that the sa'y stops at Marwah, not that the running continues to it. On Marwah, the pilgrim does as on Safa: takbir, tahlil, salawat, dua, and raising hands. The author then quotes the matn that after sa'y, the pilgrim stays in Makkah as muhrim, performs tawaf whenever he wishes, and prays two rak'ahs per tawaf. Then the commentary adds a caution against al-Tahawi, who held that sa'y should start and end at Safa, making 14 circuits. The author refutes this as incorrect. The correct Hanafi view is that sa'y consists of seven circuits, each from Safa to Marwah.

Key Terms
الميلين الأخضرين (al-milayn al-akhḍarayn): Two markers, one green and one red, carved from the wall of the Masjid al-Haram, indicating the place of quick pacing during sa'y.
بطن الوادي (baṭn al-wādī): The bottom of the valley between Safa and Marwah, where the pilgrim runs quickly between the two markers.
شوط (shawṭ): One complete circuit of sa'y from Safa to Marwah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentary, what is the correct starting and ending point of sa'y?
A) Start at Safa, end at Safa
B) Start at Marwah, end at Safa
C) Start at Safa, end at Marwah
D) Start at Marwah, end at Marwah

Key Takeaway
Sa'y is seven circuits from Safa to Marwah; the minority view of ending at Safa is rejected as incorrect.

Voluntary Tawaf and the Two Rak'ahs After It
Ruling with proof on voluntary tawaf and the prayer after it

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on voluntary tawaf, explain why the two rak'ahs are sunnah muakkadah, and identify when combining tawafs without prayer is disliked.

Core Idea
Tawaf is like prayer in virtue; each tawaf deserves its own two rak'ahs, and combining them without prayer is makruh.

A pilgrim staying in Makkah as a muhrim may perform voluntary tawaf whenever he wishes. The Hanafi school emphasizes that tawaf resembles prayer in merit, as the Prophet ﷺ said: 'Circumambulation of the House is prayer.' Consequently, after each complete circuit of seven rounds, it is recommended to pray two rak'ahs. Combining two or more tawafs without the intervening prayer is considered makruh tanzihi by Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what the passage rules upon: voluntary tawaf is allowed anytime for the muhrim; two rak'ahs after each tawaf are sunnah muakkadah; combining tawafs without prayer is makruh.
The ruling on tawaf itself: mustahabb (recommended). The two rak'ahs: sunnah muakkadah.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof quoted is the hadith 'الطواف بالبيت صلاة' (circumambulation of the House is prayer).
Reference: Sunan al-Tirmidhi (960), Al-Hakim in al-Mustadrak.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith equates tawaf to prayer in virtue and legal effect. Therefore, just as prayer is the best of deeds and requires separation between units, tawaf also merits a prayer after it, and combining tawafs without prayer is disliked.
The parallelism: al-'illa is the shared resemblance to prayer.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The dislike (karahah) of combining tawafs without prayer is the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. The view of Abu Yusuf is not mentioned here; other schools may not hold this dislike.
Within Hanafi, the mufta bihi is the dislike.
5
Apply the ruling to practice
For visitors (ghuraba'), tawaf is better than prayer because they can only do it in Makkah; for residents, prayer is better. After each tawaf, one should pray two rak'ahs, and not combine multiple tawafs without praying between them.
Sa'y is not repeated after voluntary tawafs – it is only once for Hajj/Umrah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ثم يقيم بمكة حراماً، يطوف بالبيت كلما بدا له؛ لأنه يُشبه قال عليه الصلاة والسلام: «الطواف بالبيت صلاة». والصلاة خير موضوع، فكذا الطواف، إلا أنه لا يسعى عقيب هذه الأطوفة؛ لأن السعي لا يجب إلا مرة، والتنفل به غير مشروع. - وإنما قال: يطوف بالبيت كلَّما بدا له: لينبه بهذا على أن الطواف للغرباء أفضل من الصلاة، ولأهل مكة الصلاة أفضل منه؛ لأن الغرباء يفوتهم الطواف إذا رجعوا إلى بلادهم ولا تفوتهم الصلاة، وأهل مكة: لا يفوتهم الأمران، ن، وعند اجتماعهما : فالصلاة أفضل. قوله: ( ويصلي لكل أسبوع ركعتين)، وهما ركعتا الطواف. ويكره الجمع بين أسبوعين أو أكثر من غير صلاة بينهما عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد، سواء انصرف عن وتر أو شفع ؛ لأن الركعتين مرتبتان على الطواف.
His saying: (Then he stays in Makkah as a muhrim, circumambulating the House whenever he wishes, because it is similar to what he, peace be upon him, said: 'Circumambulation of the House is prayer.') And prayer is the best of deeds, so likewise is tawaf, except that he does not perform sa'y after these tawafs because sa'y is only obligatory once, and supererogatory sa'y is not prescribed. - And he said: 'he circumambulates the House whenever he wishes' to indicate that for visitors, tawaf is better than prayer, and for the people of Makkah, prayer is better than tawaf; because visitors will miss tawaf when they return to their lands and they do not miss prayer, while the people of Makkah do not miss either. And when both are present, prayer is better. His saying: (He prays two rak'ahs for each seven circuits), and these are the two rak'ahs of tawaf. It is disliked to combine two or more circuits without prayer between them according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, whether he concludes with odd or even, because the two rak'ahs are attached to the tawaf.
Source pages p. 350

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding voluntary tawaf during the stay in Makkah as a muhrim. The matn states that the pilgrim stays in Makkah and may perform tawaf whenever he wishes. The commentator provides the proof: the Prophet said, 'Circumambulation of the House is prayer,' meaning it resembles prayer in virtue. Since prayer is the best act, tawaf is also excellent. However, sa'y is not performed after these voluntary tawafs because sa'y is only obligatory once in Hajj or Umrah; supererogatory sa'y is not legislated. The author then explains that for visitors (ghuraba'), tawaf is better than prayer because they can perform tawaf only while in Makkah, whereas prayer is possible everywhere. For residents of Makkah, prayer is better because they can perform tawaf anytime. Then the matn continues: he prays two rak'ahs after each seven circuits (i.e., each tawaf). The commentator adds that it is disliked (makruh) to combine two or more tawafs without praying between them, according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. This is because the two rak'ahs are attached to each tawaf, similar to how prayer is attached to it per the hadith. The dislike applies whether one finishes an odd number or even number of tawafs.

Key Terms
الطواف (al-ṭawāf): Circumambulation of the Ka'bah seven times, performed voluntarily or as part of Hajj/Umrah.
الركعتان (al-rak'atān): The two rak'ahs of prayer offered after each complete seven circuits of tawaf.
الجمع (al-jam'): Combining two or more tawafs without performing the two rak'ahs between them.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling regarding combining two tawafs without praying between them according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad?
A) Permissible without dislike
B) Disliked (makruh)
C) Forbidden (haram)
D) Recommended (mandub)

Key Takeaway
Voluntary tawaf is meritorious like prayer; each tawaf requires its own two rak'ahs, and combining tawafs without prayer is disliked.

Rulings on Tawaf and Combining Multiple Tawafs
Intra-Hanafi dispute on combining tawafs without prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the two rak'ahs after tawaf and identify the intra-Hanafi disagreement on combining tawafs without prayer.

Core Idea
Combining tawafs without prayer is makruh according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad; Abu Yusuf permits it on odd numbers.

This passage from al-Jawharah al-Nayrah discusses the virtue of tawaf, comparing it to prayer, and establishes that two rak'ahs must be prayed after each tawaf. It then presents a point of disagreement within the Hanafi school: can one perform multiple tawafs consecutively without praying in between? Understanding this dispute clarifies the school's reliance on the linkage between the tawaf and its prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act under discussion? Performing two or more tawafs without the intervening two rak'ahs. What is the default ruling of the two rak'ahs? They are wajib
The two rak'ahs are linked (مرتبتان) to each tawaf.
2
State the majority Hanafi position
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold that combining two or more tawafs without prayer is makruh, regardless of whether the total number of tawafs is odd or even.
Their proof: each tawaf has its own linked prayer, so skipping it is improper.
3
Identify the dissenting view
Abu Yusuf argues that if one finishes on an odd number (e.g., 3,5,7 tawafs), the last tawaf's prayer can be paired with it, so combining is not makruh.
He focuses on the pairing of an odd number with its prayer.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical consequence? If someone performs three tawafs straight, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say makruh; Abu Yusuf says not makruh. The mufta bihi is the majority view.
The difference applies only when it is not a time of prayer prohibition.
5
Apply the exception
If the prayer time is makruh (e.g., sunrise, noon, sunset), all agree that delaying the prayer is not makruh, so combining tawafs is permissible.
The dispute is only when the prayer would be valid immediately.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(1) قلت: الذي في مختصر الطحاوي: أنه يبدأ بالصفا، ويختم بالمروة. (2) سنن الترمذي (960)، المستدرك للحاكم 495/1، وصححه ابن الملقن في البدر المنير 411/4، وتوسع في ذكر طرقه، ورد على من ضعفه.
Then he resides in Mecca as a muhrim, performing tawaf around the House whenever he wishes, and praying two rak'ahs for each tawaf (seven circuits). This is a precaution against the statement of al-Tahawi, for he said: one begins with al-Safa and ends with al-Safa, so according to his statement it would be fourteen times, and that is incorrect. He said: (Then he resides in Mecca as a muhrim, performing tawaf around the House whenever he wishes; because it resembles prayer. The Prophet ﷺ said: 'Tawaf around the House is prayer.' And prayer is the best of deeds, so likewise is tawaf, except that one does not perform sa'y after these tawafs, because sa'y is obligatory only once, and performing it as supererogatory is not legislated. And he said: performing tawaf around the House whenever he wishes in order to indicate that tawaf is better than prayer for strangers (nonresidents), while for the people of Mecca, prayer is better than it; because strangers miss tawaf when they return to their countries, while they do not miss prayer, while for the people of Mecca, both are not missed, so when both are present, prayer is better. He said: (And he prays two rak'ahs for each tawaf), these are the two rak'ahs of tawaf. And it is disliked (makruh) to combine two or more tawafs without prayer between them according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, whether one finishes on an odd or even number, because the two rak'ahs are linked to the tawaf. Abu Yusuf said: it is not disliked if one finishes on an odd number, such as finishing on three, five, or seven tawafs. This disagreement is when it is not an disliked time; as for a disliked time, it is not disliked by consensus, and he delays the two rak'ahs of tawaf to a permissible time. (1) I say: what is in Mukhtasar al-Tahawi is that he begins with al-Safa and ends with al-Marwah. (2) Sunan al-Tirmidhi (960), al-Mustadrak of al-Hakim 1/495, and authenticated by Ibn al-Mulaqqin in al-Badr al-Munir 4/411, and he expanded on its chains and refuted those who weakened it.
Source pages p. 350

Commentary
This passage from al-Jawharah al-Nayrah discusses rulings related to tawaf and the prayer after it. The author first states that the pilgrim remains in Mecca as a muhrim and may perform tawaf whenever he wishes, praying two rak'ahs for each seven circuits (tawaf). He notes that this contradicts al-Tahawi's view that one should begin and end at al-Safa, which would make it fourteen circuits; the correct view is to begin at Safa and end at Marwah. The author then explains the hadith 'Tawaf is prayer' to show its virtue, but clarifies that tawaf is superior for non-Meccans because they may miss the opportunity to perform it after returning home, while prayer is always available. For Meccans, prayer is better since both are accessible. The two rak'ahs after tawaf are wajib (obligatory) according to the Hanafi school. Then there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad consider it makruh (disliked) to perform two or more tawafs consecutively without praying between them, regardless of whether the number of circuits is odd or even. Abu Yusuf holds that it is not makruh if the number is odd (e.g., three, five, or seven tawafs). The difference applies only when the prayer time is permissible; if the prayer is in a disliked time (such as sunrise, noon, or sunset), all agree it is not disliked to delay the prayer until a permissible time. The footnotes provide the source of the hadith and clarify al-Tahawi's position.

Key Terms
الطواف (al-tawaf): Circumambulation of the Kaaba seven times, an act of worship.
ركعتا الطواف (rak'ata al-tawaf): The two rak'ahs prayed after each tawaf.
الجمع بين الأسبوعين (al-jam' bayn al-usbu'ayn): Performing two or more tawafs without praying the two rak'ahs between them.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on performing four tawafs consecutively without praying between them?
A) Permissible (mubah)
B) Disliked (makruh)
C) Prohibited (haram)
D) Obligatory (wajib)

Key Takeaway
The two rak'ahs after each tawaf are wajib; combining tawafs without them is makruh according to the majority of the Hanafi school.

The First Hajj Sermon and Rulings of Mina
Describes first sermon and rulings for Mina

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the timing and content of the first Hajj sermon and identify the Hanafi rulings on praying and staying overnight in Mina.

Core Idea
First Hajj sermon teaches rites; praying five prayers in Mina is mustahab, staying overnight is sunnah.

This passage from al-Jawharah al-Nayrah describes the first of the three Hajj sermons, delivered on the 7th of Dhul Hijjah. It explains the Imam's role in teaching pilgrims about proceeding to Mina, praying at Arafat, standing (wuquf), and departure (ifada). The text also clarifies the geographical status of Mina and Arafat and gives specific rulings on actions in Mina: praying all five daily prayers is recommended (mustahab) and spending the night (mabit) is sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the timing and content of the first sermon
The sermon is delivered on the 7th of Dhul Hijjah, one day before the Day of Tarwiyah (8th). The Imam teaches pilgrims about going out to Mina, praying at Arafat, standing, and the departure (ifada).
There is a difference of opinion: some say after Zuhr, others before.
2
Distinguish between Mina and Arafat
Mina is a village within the Haram boundaries, one farsakh from Mecca. Arafat is outside the Haram (al-Hil), about three or four farsakhs from Mecca. Arafat is venerated by using the plural form 'Arafat'.
Mina is where sacrifices are shed; Arafat is where the essential standing occurs.
3
State the rulings for actions in Mina
The text states: 'It is mustahab to pray the five prayers there (in Mina). The overnight stay (mabit) is sunnah.' These are based on the Prophet's practice.
Mustahab means recommended; sunnah means established practice but not obligatory.
4
Note the sequence of three sermons
This is the first of three sermons in Hajj. The second is delivered on the Day of Arafat (9th) and the third on the Day of Nahr (10th) or the days of Tashriq.
Each sermon has specific content teaching the rites for that stage.

Source Text

So when it is one day before the Day of al-Tarwiyah (the 8th of Dhul Hijjah), the Imam delivers a sermon to the people, teaching them about going out to Mina, praying at Arafat, standing, and departure (ifada). Commentary
This passage from al-Jawharah al-Nayrah explains the first of the three sermons in Hajj, delivered on the 7th of Dhul Hijjah (the day before the Day of Tarwiyah). The Imam teaches the pilgrims about proceeding to Mina, the prayer at Arafat on the 9th, the standing (wuquf) at Arafat, and the departure (ifada) to Muzdalifah. There is a difference of opinion on whether this sermon is before or after Zuhr; the author mentions both views. The text then describes Mina and Arafat: Arafat is outside the Haram (in al-Hil), about three or four farsakhs from Mecca; Mina is within the Haram, one farsakh from Mecca, and is called Mina because blood of sacrifices is shed there. It is mustahab to pray all five daily prayers in Mina when staying there, and spending the night (mabit) there is sunnah. This sermon is the first of three: the second is on the day of Arafat (9th) and the third on the 10th (Yawm al-Nahr) or the following days.

Key Terms
خطبة (khutbah): Sermon delivered by the Imam on the 7th of Dhul Hijjah teaching the rites.
منى (Mina): A village within the Haram limits where pilgrims stay during the days of Tashriq.
عرفات ('Arafat): The plain outside the Haram where standing (wuquf) on the 9th is the essential part of Hajj.
المبيت (al-mabit): Spending the night in Mina on the nights of Tashriq.

The Three Sermons of Hajj and Going Out to Mina
Rulings on the three sermons and going out to Mina

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended days and times for the three Hajj sermons and explain the timing for going to Mina, including the intra-Hanafi dispute on consecutive sermons.

Core Idea
The first Hajj sermon is on the 7th, the second before Zuhr on the 9th, and the third after Zuhr on the 11th; going to Mina is recommended after sunrise on the 8th.

This lesson covers two connected practices: the three sermons (khutab) that the Imam delivers during Hajj, and the recommended timing for leaving Mecca to Mina. The author of al-Jawhara al-Nayyirah expands on al-Quduri's text, clarifying the days and times, and noting an intra-Hanafi disagreement with Zufar. Understanding these details ensures the pilgrim follows the Prophet's sunnah and avoids timing errors.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three sermons and their days
First sermon on the 7th of Dhul-Hijjah (one day before Yawm al-Tarwiyah), second sermon at Arafah on the 9th, third sermon at Mina on the 11th.
The first is instructional; second and third are like Jumu'ah sermons.
2
Note the timing relative to Zuhr prayer
First and third sermons are after Zuhr; the second (at Arafah) is two sermons before Zuhr. All are after midday except the Arafah sermons, which are before Zuhr.
Delivering before midday is permissible but disliked (makruh tanzihan) for the first and third, unlike Jumu'ah where it invalidates.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Zufar holds that sermons should be on three consecutive days: 8th, 9th, and 10th. The majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) separate them by a day (7th, 9th, 11th).
The majority view is mufta bihi because it is based on established practice.
4
Apply the recommendation for going to Mina
The pilgrim should pray Fajr in Mecca on the 8th (Yawm al-Tarwiyah) and then go to Mina after sunrise, following the Prophet's example.
The hadith from Sahih Muslim (1218) supports this.

Source pages p. 351

Commentary
This passage from al-Jawhara al-Nayyirah explains the three sermons (khutab) of Hajj and the recommended timing for going to Mina on the Day of Tarwiyah. The commentary expands on the base text of al-Quduri. First, it clarifies that the first sermon is delivered on the seventh day of Dhul-Hijjah, one day before the Day of Tarwiyah (the 8th). The Imam teaches the pilgrims about the rites: going to Mina, praying at Arafat, standing (wuquf), and the departure (ifada) from Arafat. There is a brief mention of a difference of opinion between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf regarding the timing of something related to witr prayer; the text states Abu Yusuf considers it not disliked to turn away from witr after odd cycles (3, 5, 7 etc.), but the context is unclear and likely refers to delaying certain prayers. The author notes that this difference only applies when it is not a disliked time; by consensus, during a disliked time, performing it is not disliked and one delays the two rak'ahs of tawaf. Then the passage describes the three sermons in detail: the first on the 7th (after Zuhr according to the text, though some say before Zuhr), the second at Arafah on the 9th (two sermons before Zuhr prayer, with a sitting between them like Jumu'ah), and the third at Mina on the 11th (one sermon after Zuhr prayer). Zufar disagrees, stating sermons on three consecutive days (8th, 9th, 11th). All sermons are after Zuhr except the Arafah sermon which is before Zuhr. Delivering the sermon before midday is permissible but disliked, unlike Jumu'ah where it would invalidate the prayer. Finally, regarding going out to Mina, it is recommended to pray Fajr in Mecca on the 8th and then go to Mina after sunrise, following the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) who did so and prayed five prayers there before going to Arafat. This is supported by a hadith from Sahih Muslim.

Key Terms
خطبة (khutbah): A sermon delivered by the Imam during Hajj; the first is instructional, the second and third are similar to Friday sermons but with adjusted rulings on timing.
يوم التروية (yawm al-tarwiyah): The 8th day of Dhul-Hijjah, when pilgrims traditionally prepared water (tarwiyah) and traveled to Mina.
عرفات (Arafat): The plain where the central standing (wuquf) of Hajj occurs; the text uses the plural form for glorification.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The three Hajj sermons have specific timings: first on 7th after Zuhr, second on 9th before Zuhr, third on 11th after Zuhr; and going to Mina on 8th after sunrise is recommended.
