Rulings on the Hajj Khutbahs: Timing, Number, and Intra-Madhhab Dispute
Ruling with proof and intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings for the Hajj khutbahs on the days of Tarwiyah, Arafah, and Nahr, and explain the difference between the Hanafi majority and Zufar's view.

Core Idea
The Hajj khutbahs are wajib, but their timing and number differ: two at Arafah before Zuhr, one at Mina after Zuhr, with a gap between each.

The passage from Al-Jawhara al-Nayra clarifies the sequence and rulings of the khutbahs during Hajj. Understanding these rules ensures that the rites are performed correctly according to the Hanafi school, and also highlights a subtle intra-madhhab dispute between the majority and Zufar regarding the consecutiveness of these sermons.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three khutbahs and their days
Locate in the passage the specific days and locations for the three khutbahs: the first on Yawm al-Tarwiyah (8th) at Mina, the second on Yawm 'Arafah (9th) at 'Arafat, and the third on Yawm al-Nahr (11th) at Mina.
Note the gap: between the first and second there is one day (9th), and between second and third there is one day (10th), as per the majority view.
2
Note the timing relative to Zuhr prayer
Observe that the first and third khutbahs are after Zuhr, while the second (on 'Arafah) is before Zuhr. This is a key distinction from Jumu'ah where the khutbah is always before prayer.
The passage states: 'كل هذه الخطب بعد الزوال بعد صلاة الظهر إلا يوم عرفة'.
3
Understand the ruling if delivered before zawal
The passage says that delivering the khutbah before zawal (sun's decline) is permissible but makruh, unlike Jumu'ah where it would invalidate the prayer. This shows the difference in strictness.
The text: 'ولو خطب قبل الزوال جاز ويكره بخلاف الجمعة'.
4
Compare with Jumu'ah khutbah
Consider why Jumu'ah is stricter: it has a fixed time window before Zuhr, while the Hajj khutbah can be earlier but is disliked. This relates to the nature of worship.
Jumu'ah is a weekly obligation with specific conditions; Hajj is an annual pilgrimage with more flexibility.
5
Examine Zufar's dissenting view and thamarah al-khilaf
Zufar opines that the khutbahs should be on three consecutive days (8th, 9th, 10th). The majority hold there is a gap. The practical difference: if one follows Zufar, the third khutbah would be on the 10th (Yawm al-Nahr) instead of the 11th.
The passage: 'وقال زفر: يخطب في ثلاثة أيام متواليات يوم التروية ويوم عرفة ويوم النحر.'

Source Text

كتاب الحج

فإذا صلى الفجر يومَ التروية بمكة : خَرَجَ إلى منى، فأقام بهـا حـتى يصلي الفجر يوم عرفة .

والثانية : بعرفة يوم عرفة خطبتين قبل صلاة الظهر، يجلس بينهما كما في الجمعة.
والثالثة : بمنى، يوم الحادي عشر خطبة واحدة بعد صلاة الظهر،
يفصل بين كل خطبتين بيوم.
وقال زفر: يخطب في ثلاثة أيام متواليات يوم التروية، ويوم عرفة، ويوم النحر.
وكل هذه الخطب : بعد الزوال بعد صلاة الظهر، إلا يوم عرفة: فإن الخطبتين فيه قبل الصلاة.
ولو خطب قبل الزوال : جاز، ويكره بخلاف الجمعة: فإنه إذا ترك الخطبة فيها، أو خطب قبل الزوال: لا يجوز.

[الخروج إلى منى :]
* قوله : (فإذا صلى الفجر بمكة يوم التروية : خرج إلى منى، فأقام بها حتى يصلي الفجر من يوم عرفة).
والمستحب أن يكون خروجه بعد طلوع الشمس؛ لأن النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام خرج إلى منى بعد طلوع الشمس، فصلى بها الظهر والعصر والمغرب والعشاء والفجر، ثم راح إلى عرفات (۱).
(۱) صحیح مسلم (۱۲۱۸).

ثم يتوجه إلى عرفات، فيقيم بها .
فإذا زالت الشمس من يوم عرفة : صلى الإمام بالناس الظهر والعصر. يبتدى فيخطبُ خُطبتين قبل الصلاة، يعلم الناس فيهما الصلاة، والوقوف بعرفة، وبالمزدلفة، ورمي الجمار ، والنحر، والحلق، وطواف الزيارة.
ولو بات بمكة ليلة عرفة وصلى بها الفجر، ثم غدا إلى عرفات، ومر بمني أجزاء، ويكون مسيئاً.

الذهاب إلى عرفات :]
قوله : (ثم يتوجه إلى عرفات، فيقيم بها.
والمستحب أن يكون توجهه بعد طلوع الشمس، فإذا بلغ إلى عرفة: أقام بها حيث أحب إلا بطن عُرَنة، ويكره أن ينزل في موضع وحده. * قوله: (فإذا زالت الشمس من يوم عرفة : صلى الإمام بالناس الظهر والعصر بأذان واحد، وإقامتين)، ولا يجهر فيهما بالقراءة؛ لأنهما صلاتا نهار، كسائر الأيام. قوله: (يبتدئ فيخطب خطبتين، يُعلم الناس فيهما الصلاة، والوقوف بعرفة، وبالمزدلفة، ورمي الجمار، والنحر، والحلق، وطواف الزيارة)، قائماً، ويفصل بينهما بجلسة خفيفة، كما في الجمعة، فإذا فرغ من الخطبة: أقام المؤذن.
وإن خطب قاعداً أجزأه إلا أن القيام أفضل؛ لأن المقصود تعليم الناس، وتبليغهم، والقيام: أمكن في ذلك.
The Book of Hajj. When he prays Fajr on the day of Tarwiyah in Makkah, he goes out to Mina and stays there until he prays Fajr on the day of Arafah. The second: at Arafah on the day of Arafah, two sermons before the Zuhr prayer, sitting between them as in Jumu'ah. The third: at Mina on the eleventh day, one sermon after Zuhr prayer. There is a separation of one day between every two sermons. And Zufar said: He delivers sermons on three consecutive days: the day of Tarwiyah, the day of Arafah, and the day of Nahr. All these sermons are after zawal (decline of the sun) after Zuhr prayer, except the day of Arafah: the two sermons are before the prayer. If he delivered the sermon before zawal, it is permissible but disliked (makruh), contrary to Jumu'ah: if he misses the sermon in it, or delivers the sermon before zawal, it is not valid. [Departure to Mina:] His saying: (When he prays Fajr in Makkah on the day of Tarwiyah, he goes out to Mina and stays there until he prays Fajr on the day of Arafah.) It is mustahabb that his departure be after sunrise, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) went out to Mina after sunrise, then prayed Zuhr, Asr, Maghrib, Isha, and Fajr there, then went to Arafat. (Saheeh Muslim 1218). Then he proceeds to Arafat and stays there. When the sun has declined on the day of Arafah, the Imam leads the people in Zuhr and Asr. He begins and delivers two sermons before the prayer, teaching the people about the prayer, the standing at Arafah, at Muzdalifah, throwing the stones, the sacrifice, shaving, and the Tawaf al-Ziyarah. If he spends the night of Arafah in Makkah and prays Fajr there, then goes to Arafat passing through Mina, it suffices him but he is considered negligent. [Going to Arafat:] His saying: (Then he proceeds to Arafat and stays there.) It is mustahabb that he proceed after sunrise. When he reaches Arafah, he stays where he likes except the valley of Uranah, and it is disliked (makruh) to stay alone in a place. His saying: (When the sun has declined on the day of Arafah, the Imam leads the people in Zuhr and Asr with one adhan and two iqamas), and he does not recite loudly in them because they are daytime prayers like other days. His saying: (He begins and delivers two sermons, teaching the people about the prayer, the standing at Arafah, at Muzdalifah, throwing the stones, the sacrifice, shaving, and the Tawaf al-Ziyarah), standing, and he separates them with a short sitting as in Jumu'ah. When he finishes the sermon, the mu'adhdhin gives the iqamah. If he delivers the sermon sitting, it suffices him but standing is better because the purpose is to teach the people and convey to them, and standing is more effective in that.
Source pages p. 352

Commentary
This is a commentary on the matn of Al-Quduri dealing with the rites of Hajj from the 8th to the 10th of Dhul Hijjah. The passage type is a ruling with proof and an intra-Hanafi dispute. The author first states the rulings for the khutbahs: on the 8th (day of Tarwiyah) at Mina, one sermon after Zuhr; on the 9th (day of Arafah) at Arafah, two sermons before Zuhr; on the 11th (day of Nahr) at Mina, one sermon after Zuhr. There is a separation of one day between each set. Then he mentions Zufar's opinion that the sermons are on three consecutive days: 8th, 9th, and 10th (day of Nahr). This is an intra-Hanafi dispute. He clarifies that all sermons are after zawal and after Zuhr except for the day of Arafah where the two sermons are before Zuhr. He then discusses the ruling if the sermon is delivered before zawal: it is permissible but makruh, unlike Jumu'ah where it would invalidate the prayer. The commentary then explains the departure to Mina: it is mustahabb to depart after sunset, as the Prophet did. He proceeds to stay in Mina until after Fajr of the 9th, then goes to Arafat. On the day of Arafah, when the sun declines, the Imam leads a combined Zuhr and Asr prayer with one adhan and two iqamas, without loud recitation. He then delivers two sermons standing, teaching the rites. If he preaches sitting, it is valid but standing is better. If someone spends the night of Arafah in Makkah and goes directly to Arafat via Mina, it is valid but makruh. The commentary also notes that it is makruh to stay in the valley of Uranah.

Key Terms
خُطبة (khutbah): The sermon delivered during Hajj on specific days, consisting of reminders and teachings about the rites.
زوال (zawal): The time when the sun passes its zenith and begins to decline, marking the start of Zuhr prayer time.
عرفة (Arafah): The 9th day of Dhul Hijjah; the standing at Arafat is the most essential pillar of Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if the Imam delivers the Hajj khutbah on the day of Tarwiyah before zawal (noon)?
A) It is invalid, like in Jumu'ah.
B) It is permissible but disliked (makruh).
C) It is recommended (mustahabb).
D) It is prohibited (haram).

Key Takeaway
The Hajj khutbahs are wajib with specific timings; the majority Hanafi view is that they are spaced out (8th, 9th, 11th), and delivering them before zawal is valid but makruh.

Hajj — Pilgrimage

The Imam's Actions at 'Arafah and Combining Prayers
Explanation of imam's actions at 'Arafah and procedure for combining prayers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the sequence of actions performed by the imam at 'Arafah on the day of 'Arafah and identify the correct method for combining Dhuhr and 'Asr.

Core Idea
At 'Arafah, the imam delivers two sermons and combines Dhuhr and 'Asr with one adhan and two iqamas – a concession unique to Hajj.

The day of 'Arafah is the climax of Hajj. The imam leads the pilgrims in a prescribed sequence of actions that includes delivering two sermons and combining the Dhuhr and 'Asr prayers. This lesson walks you through the recommended procedure and the rulings on deviations.

Guided Path
1
Follow the Imām's Schedule
Start from the time after sunrise to the sunset. The imam proceeds to 'Arafah, stays, and when the sun declines, he delivers two sermons before the prayer.
The imam should deliver the sermons after the sun has declined (zawal).
2
Examine the Sermon Content
The sermons teach the key rituals: prayer, standing at 'Arafah, Muzdalifah, stoning, sacrifice, shaving, and Tawaf al-Ziyarah.
The sermons are primarily instructional.
3
Understand the Combination Procedure
The imam prays Dhuhr and 'Asr with one adhan and two iqamas, reciting silently, no supererogatory prayer between them.
No loud recitation because these are daytime prayers.
4
Deal with Omissions
If the sermon is omitted or given before noon, the combination still suffices but is blameworthy.
The combination itself is not invalidated by these omissions.

الذهاب إلى عرفات :] قوله : (ثم يتوجه إلى عرفات، فيقيم بها. والمستحب أن يكون توجهه بعد طلوع الشمس، فإذا بلغ إلى عرفة: أقام بها حيث أحب إلا بطن عُرَنة، ويكره أن ينزل في موضع وحده. * قوله: (فإذا زالت الشمس من يوم عرفة : صلى الإمام بالناس الظهر والعصر بأذان واحد، وإقامتين)، ولا يجهر فيهما بالقراءة؛ لأنهما صلاتا نهار، كسائر الأيام. قوله: (يبتدئ فيخطب خطبتين، يُعلم الناس فيهما الصلاة، والوقوف بعرفة، وبالمزدلفة، ورمي الجمار، والنحر، والحلق، وطواف الزيارة)، قائماً، ويفصل بينهما بجلسة خفيفة، كما في الجمعة، فإذا فرغ من الخطبة: أقام المؤذن. وإن خطب قاعداً أجزأه إلا أن القيام أفضل؛ لأن المقصود تعليم الناس، وتبليغهم، والقيام: أمكن في ذلك.

ويصلي بهم الظهر والعصر في وقت الظهر بأذان، وإقامتين . وإن ترك الخطبة، أو خَطَبَ قبل الزوال : أجزأه، وقد أساء. * قوله : ( ويصلي بهم الظهر والعصر في وقت الظهر بأذان وإقامتين). ثم إذا فرغ من صلاة الظهر : أقام المؤذِّن للعصر؛ لأنها تُؤدى قبل وقتها المعهود، فيُفرد لها إقامة؛ إعلاماً للناس بها. ولا يتطوع بين الصلاتين، فإن تطوع بغير سنة الظهر، أو اشتغل بعمل آخر من أكل أو شرب: أعاد الأذان للعصر. وعن محمد : لا يعيده، وتجزئه الإقامة. قال في الوجيز»: أما سنَّة الظهر الراتبة إذا صلاها: لا تفصل، ولا يعاد الأذان إذا اشتغل بها.

ثم اعلم أن شرائط جواز الجمع عند أبي حنيفة خمسة: الوقت والمكان، والإحرام، والإمام، والجماعة. وعندهما: الإمام والجماعة ليسا بشرط.

If he omits the sermon or delivers it before noon, it suffices, but he has done wrong. * His statement: (And he prays Dhuhr and 'Asr with them in the time of Dhuhr with one adhan and two iqamas.) Then when he finishes the Dhuhr prayer, the mu'adhdhin gives the iqama for 'Asr because it is performed before its usual time, so a separate iqama is given to inform the people. No supererogatory prayer is performed between the two prayers. If he performs a supererogatory prayer other than the sunnah of Dhuhr, or engages in another action like eating or drinking, he repeats the adhan for 'Asr. According to Muhammad: he does not repeat it, and the iqama suffices. Al-Wajiz says: As for the regular sunnah of Dhuhr, if he prays it, it does not separate, and the adhan is not repeated if he engages in it. Then know that the conditions for the permissibility of combining (jam') according to Abu Hanifa are five: time, place, ihram, imam, and congregation. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): imam and congregation are not conditions. Then ihram is necessary before noon, as a precondition for combining. If he assumes ihram after noon, there are two transmissions from Abu Hanifa: one is that it is not permissible for him to combine, so that if he prays Dhuhr with the imam before assuming ihram for Hajj, then assumes ihram before 'Asr, it is not permissible for him to combine. It is only permissible if he prays both prayers while being in the state of ihram for Hajj.
Source pages p. 353

Commentary
This passage from 'Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah' explains the rituals at 'Arafah on the day of 'Arafah, focusing on the imam's actions and the combination of Dhuhr and 'Asr prayers. It begins as a ruling statement: after proceeding to 'Arafah, when the sun declines, the imam delivers two sermons (khutbahs) teaching the pilgrims about the key rituals, then leads them in Dhuhr and 'Asr combined with one adhan and two iqamas, reciting silently. The commentary clarifies that standing during the sermon is preferred but not obligatory. It then addresses cases where the sermon is omitted or given before noon, which still suffices but is blameworthy. The passage transitions into an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the conditions for combining prayers (jam'). According to Abu Hanifa, five conditions are required: (1) time (the combined time of Dhuhr), (2) place ('Arafah), (3) ihram (state of consecration for Hajj), (4) imam (leading the congregation), and (5) congregation (being in a group). The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that imam and congregation are not conditions; combining is permissible even for an individual praying alone at 'Arafah while in ihram. Furthermore, a dispute is reported from Abu Hanifa himself about the timing of ihram: if one assumes ihram after noon, there are two opinions—one allowing combination only if one was in ihram before the Dhuhr prayer, and another restricting it. The relied-upon view is that ihram must precede noon for the combining to be valid. The practical consequence is that a pilgrim arriving late at 'Arafah must still combine if in ihram, but if not, they pray each prayer separately.

Key Terms
الجمع (al-jam‘): Performing two prayers (Dhuhr and 'Asr) in the same time at 'Arafah, which is a concession specific to Hajj.
الإحرام (al-ihram): The state of consecration for Hajj or 'Umrah, initiated by wearing the ihram garments and making the intention, accompanied by the talbiyah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if the imam delivers the sermon before the sun declines?
A) Invalid; must repeat.
B) Valid but blameworthy.
C) Valid and recommended.
D) Invalid and he must lead again.

Key Takeaway
The combination of Dhuhr and 'Asr at 'Arafah with two sermons and silent recitation is a sunnah established by the Prophet (peace be upon him); deviations are allowed but discouraged.

Conditions for Combining at 'Arafah: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute over conditions for combining prayers at 'Arafah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the five conditions for combining at 'Arafah according to Abu Hanifa, distinguish the Sahibayn’s position, and apply the practical consequence to a lone pilgrim.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa requires imam and congregation for combining; the Sahibayn do not – the practical difference is a pilgrim alone.

The combination of prayers at 'Arafah is a concession, but its validity depends on conditions. The Hanafi school has an internal dispute on two conditions: the presence of an imam and a congregation. This lesson examines the arguments and the operative fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Five Conditions
According to Abu Hanifa, five conditions are required: time (zawal), place ('Arafah), ihram (state of consecration for Hajj), imam (a leader), and congregation (a group).
The Sahibayn agree on time, place, and ihram, but not imam and congregation.
2
Note the Dispute
Abu Hanifa holds that imam and congregation are necessary; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold they are not.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
3
Understand the Reasoning
Abu Hanifa's reasoning is based on the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) who led the people in congregation, and analogy to Friday prayer which requires congregation. The Sahibayn argue that the essence of the concession (rukhsah) is the time and place, not the congregation.
The text does not elaborate extensively on the dalil, but the underlying principle is that the concession is primarily linked to the specific time and place.
4
Apply the Practical Consequence
If a pilgrim is alone at 'Arafah, according to Abu Hanifa he cannot combine (must pray each separately), while according to the Sahibayn he can combine.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference).
5
Recognize the Mufta Bihi
The relied-upon position for fatwa is that of the Sahibayn, as it is more accommodating and aligned with the ease of travel.
The text does not explicitly state tarjih, but the inclusion of the Sahibayn's view without rejection implies acceptance.

Source Text

ثم يتوجه إلى عرفات، فيقيم بها . فإذا زالت الشمس من يوم عرفة : صلى الإمام بالناس الظهر والعصر. يبتدى فيخطبُ خُطبتين قبل الصلاة، يعلم الناس فيهما الصلاة، والوقوف بعرفة، وبالمزدلفة، ورمي الجمار ، والنحر، والحلق، وطواف الزيارة. ولو بات بمكة ليلة عرفة وصلى بها الفجر، ثم غدا إلى عرفات، ومر بمني أجزاء، ويكون مسيئاً.

الذهاب إلى عرفات :] قوله : (ثم يتوجه إلى عرفات، فيقيم بها. والمستحب أن يكون توجهه بعد طلوع الشمس، فإذا بلغ إلى عرفة: أقام بها حيث أحب إلا بطن عُرَنة، ويكره أن ينزل في موضع وحده. * قوله: (فإذا زالت الشمس من يوم عرفة : صلى الإمام بالناس الظهر والعصر بأذان واحد، وإقامتين)، ولا يجهر فيهما بالقراءة؛ لأنهما صلاتا نهار، كسائر الأيام. قوله: (يبتدئ فيخطب خطبتين، يُعلم الناس فيهما الصلاة، والوقوف بعرفة، وبالمزدلفة، ورمي الجمار، والنحر، والحلق، وطواف الزيارة)، قائماً، ويفصل بينهما بجلسة خفيفة، كما في الجمعة، فإذا فرغ من الخطبة: أقام المؤذن. وإن خطب قاعداً أجزأه إلا أن القيام أفضل؛ لأن المقصود تعليم الناس، وتبليغهم، والقيام: أمكن في ذلك.

ويصلي بهم الظهر والعصر في وقت الظهر بأذان، وإقامتين . وإن ترك الخطبة، أو خَطَبَ قبل الزوال : أجزأه، وقد أساء. * قوله : ( ويصلي بهم الظهر والعصر في وقت الظهر بأذان وإقامتين). ثم إذا فرغ من صلاة الظهر : أقام المؤذِّن للعصر؛ لأنها تُؤدى قبل وقتها المعهود، فيُفرد لها إقامة؛ إعلاماً للناس بها. ولا يتطوع بين الصلاتين، فإن تطوع بغير سنة الظهر، أو اشتغل بعمل آخر من أكل أو شرب: أعاد الأذان للعصر. وعن محمد : لا يعيده، وتجزئه الإقامة. قال في الوجيز»: أما سنَّة الظهر الراتبة إذا صلاها: لا تفصل، ولا يعاد الأذان إذا اشتغل بها.

ثم اعلم أن شرائط جواز الجمع عند أبي حنيفة خمسة: الوقت والمكان، والإحرام، والإمام، والجماعة. وعندهما: الإمام والجماعة ليسا بشرط.
- ثم لا بد من الإحرام قبل الزوال ؛ تقديماً للإحرام على وقت الجمع، فإن أحرم بعد الزوال : فيه روايتان عن أبي حنيفة : إحداهما : لا يجوز له الجمع، حتى لو صلى الظهر مع الإمام قبل أن يُحرم بالحج، ثم أحرم بالحج قبل العصر : لم يجز له الجمع، وإنما يجوز إذا صلى الصلاتين جميعاً وهو محرم بالحج.
Then he proceeds to 'Arafat and stays there. When the sun declines on the day of 'Arafah, the Imam leads the people in Dhuhr and 'Asr prayers. He begins by delivering two sermons before the prayer, teaching the people about the prayer, the standing at 'Arafah, at Muzdalifah, the stoning of the Jamarat, the sacrifice, the shaving, and the Tawaf al-Ziyarah. If he spends the night of 'Arafah in Makkah and prays Fajr there, then goes to 'Arafat and passes through Mina, it suffices, but he is doing wrong. Going to 'Arafat: His statement: (Then he proceeds to 'Arafat and stays there.) It is recommended that he proceed after sunrise. When he reaches 'Arafah, he stays wherever he likes except the valley of 'Uranah, and it is disliked that he alight in a place alone. * His statement: (When the sun declines on the day of 'Arafah, the Imam leads the people in Dhuhr and 'Asr with one adhan and two iqamas.) He does not recite aloud in them because they are daytime prayers like other days. His statement: (He begins by delivering two sermons, teaching the people therein about the prayer, the standing at 'Arafah, at Muzdalifah, the stoning of the Jamarat, the sacrifice, the shaving, and the Tawaf al-Ziyarah), while standing, and he separates them with a brief sitting, as in Friday. When he finishes the sermon, the mu'adhdhin gives the iqama. If he delivers the sermon sitting, it suffices, but standing is better because the purpose is to teach and convey to the people, and standing is more effective for that. And he prays Dhuhr and 'Asr with them in the time of Dhuhr with one adhan and two iqamas. If he omits the sermon or delivers it before noon, it suffices, but he has done wrong. * His statement: (And he prays Dhuhr and 'Asr with them in the time of Dhuhr with one adhan and two iqamas.) Then when he finishes the Dhuhr prayer, the mu'adhdhin gives the iqama for 'Asr because it is performed before its usual time, so a separate iqama is given to inform the people. No supererogatory prayer is performed between the two prayers. If he performs a supererogatory prayer other than the sunnah of Dhuhr, or engages in another action like eating or drinking, he repeats the adhan for 'Asr. According to Muhammad: he does not repeat it, and the iqama suffices. Al-Wajiz says: As for the regular sunnah of Dhuhr, if he prays it, it does not separate, and the adhan is not repeated if he engages in it. Then know that the conditions for the permissibility of combining (jam') according to Abu Hanifa are five: time, place, ihram, imam, and congregation. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): imam and congregation are not conditions. Then ihram is necessary before noon, as a precondition for combining. If he assumes ihram after noon, there are two transmissions from Abu Hanifa: one is that it is not permissible for him to combine, so that if he prays Dhuhr with the imam before assuming ihram for Hajj, then assumes ihram before 'Asr, it is not permissible for him to combine. It is only permissible if he prays both prayers while being in the state of ihram for Hajj.
Source pages p. 353

Commentary
This passage from 'Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah' explains the rituals at 'Arafah on the day of 'Arafah, focusing on the imam's actions and the combination of Dhuhr and 'Asr prayers. It begins as a ruling statement: after proceeding to 'Arafah, when the sun declines, the imam delivers two sermons (khutbahs) teaching the pilgrims about the key rituals, then leads them in Dhuhr and 'Asr combined with one adhan and two iqamas, reciting silently. The commentary clarifies that standing during the sermon is preferred but not obligatory. It then addresses cases where the sermon is omitted or given before noon, which still suffices but is blameworthy. The passage transitions into an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the conditions for combining prayers (jam'). According to Abu Hanifa, five conditions are required: (1) time (the combined time of Dhuhr), (2) place ('Arafah), (3) ihram (state of consecration for Hajj), (4) imam (leading the congregation), and (5) congregation (being in a group). The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that imam and congregation are not conditions; combining is permissible even for an individual praying alone at 'Arafah while in ihram. Furthermore, a dispute is reported from Abu Hanifa himself about the timing of ihram: if one assumes ihram after noon, there are two opinions—one allowing combination only if one was in ihram before the Dhuhr prayer, and another restricting it. The relied-upon view is that ihram must precede noon for the combining to be valid. The practical consequence is that a pilgrim arriving late at 'Arafah must still combine if in ihram, but if not, they pray each prayer separately.

Key Terms
الجمع (al-jam‘): Performing two prayers (Dhuhr and 'Asr) in the same time at 'Arafah, which is a concession specific to Hajj.
الإحرام (al-ihram): The state of consecration for Hajj or 'Umrah, initiated by wearing the ihram garments and making the intention, accompanied by the talbiyah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Conditions for Combining Zuhr and Asr at 'Arafat
Expands rulings on jam' between Zuhr and Asr at 'Arafat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five conditions for combining Zuhr and Asr at 'Arafat according to Abu Hanifa, explain why the Sahibayn differ, and apply the dispute to practical scenarios.

Core Idea
Combining at 'Arafat requires imam and congregation according to Abu Hanifa; the Sahibayn disagree.

This passage from Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira explores the special Hajj concession of combining Zuhr and Asr at 'Arafat. The matn describes the procedure, but the commentary reveals a significant internal Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa insists on five conditions, while his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, reduce them to three. Understanding this dispute is essential for knowing how to correctly perform this sunnah in Hajj.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is combining Zuhr and Asr at 'Arafat during Hajj. It is a sunnah act specific to this place and time. Focus on what conditions are required for it to be valid.
Combining here means offering both prayers in the time of Zuhr.
2
List Abu Hanifa's five conditions
According to the text, Abu Hanifa requires: (1) time (being after zawal at 'Arafat), (2) place ('Arafat), (3) ihram (state of pilgrimage), (4) imam (the greater imam leading Hajj), and (5) congregation (jama'ah).
The first three are agreed upon; the last two are disputed.
3
Identify the Sahibayn's objection
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that imam and congregation are not conditions. Their reasoning is that the concession is tied to the act of Hajj itself, not to the presence of a specific imam or group.
They still require time, place, and ihram.
4
Follow the dalil for both sides
Abu Hanifa cites the Quranic verse (an-Nisa 4:103) that prayer is a timed obligation, so combining is an exception limited to those following the greater imam. The Sahibayn rely on the general practice of the Prophet and the Companions at 'Arafat.
The text does not elaborate the Sahibayn's dalil explicitly; it infers from the concession being part of Hajj.
5
Determine the practical thamarah
According to Abu Hanifa, a pilgrim who prays Zuhr alone in his tent must offer each prayer in its own time. According to the Sahibayn, he may combine if he is at 'Arafat and in ihram, even if alone.
The same applies if he prays behind a local imam who is not the greater imam.

Then know that the conditions for the permissibility of combining (jam') according to Abu Hanifa are five: time, place, ihram, imam, and congregation. According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), imam and congregation are not conditions. Then ihram must be before zawal, giving precedence to ihram over the time of combining. If he enters ihram after zawal, there are two narrations from Abu Hanifa: One of them: It is not permissible for him to combine; even if he prays Zuhr with the imam before entering ihram for Hajj, then enters ihram for Hajj before Asr, combining is not permissible for him; rather it is permissible only if he prays both prayers while in the state of ihram for Hajj. And whoever prays Zuhr in his tent alone, he prays each one at its time according to Abu Hanifa. In the second narration: If he is in ihram before Asr, it suffices him; this is the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, because the performance of Zuhr at its time does not depend on the condition of ihram; rather that is needed only for advancing Asr before its time. If he prays Zuhr alone, then prays Asr with the imam, that does not suffice him according to Abu Hanifa, because the imam in his view is a condition for both prayers. If he catches with the imam one rak'ah of each of the two prayers, or something of the two prayers, combining is valid by consensus. And if the imam prays with the people on a cloudy day, then it becomes clear that he prayed Zuhr before zawal and Asr after zawal, then he repeats the khutbah and both prayers. * His statement: (And whoever prays in his tent alone, he prays each one at its time according to Abu Hanifa, because preserving the time is an obligation by textual evidence. Allah Most High said: {Indeed, prayer has been upon the believers a prescribed book, timed} (an-Nisa 4:103), i.e., an obligation with a fixed time. So it is not permissible to leave it except in what the Sacred Law has permitted, which is combining in congregation with the imam, meaning the greater imam. For whoever prays Zuhr in congregation, but not with the greater imam, combining is not permissible for him according to Abu Hanifa, like the one who prays alone.
Source pages p. 354

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the conditions for combining Zuhr and Asr at 'Arafat during Hajj. The commentator begins by quoting the matn that the imam leads both prayers in the time of Zuhr with one adhan and two iqamas. He explains that after Zuhr, a separate iqama for Asr is made because Asr is offered before its usual time. No supererogatory prayers are allowed between them; if one does, the adhan must be repeated. However, Imam Muhammad says the iqama suffices and no repeat is needed. The regular sunnah of Zuhr does not count as a separating supererogatory act. The main dispute: Abu Hanifa lists five conditions for the validity of combining: (1) time (i.e., being in the time of Zuhr at 'Arafat), (2) place (being at 'Arafat), (3) ihram (state of pilgrimage), (4) the imam (the leader of Hajj, i.e., the greater imam), and (5) congregation (jama'ah). His two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), hold that imam and congregation are not conditions. They argue that the core condition is ihram and being at the place and time. The passage then discusses the timing of ihram: according to one narration from Abu Hanifa, ihram must be before zawal; if done after, combining is invalid. The second narration (agreeing with the Sahibayn) allows ihram before Asr. If one prays Zuhr alone in his tent, he must pray each prayer in its own time according to Abu Hanifa, because preserving the time is obligatory by the Quranic verse (an-Nisa 103). Only by joining the greater imam in congregation can the time be altered. Thus, the greater imam is necessary. If one catches a rak'ah of each prayer with the imam, combining is valid by consensus. If the imam mistakenly prays early or late due to cloudy weather, he must repeat the khutbah and both prayers.

Key Terms
الجمع (al-jam'): Combining two prayers (Zuhr and Asr) at 'Arafat in the time of Zuhr, or Maghrib and 'Isha at Muzdalifah in the time of 'Isha.
الإمام الأكبر (al-imam al-akbar): The greater imam, meaning the caliph, sultan, or his specially appointed representative who leads the Hajj pilgrimage.
الإحرام (al-ihram): The state of ritual consecration for Hajj or 'Umrah, which includes wearing the ihram garments and abstaining from prohibited acts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Five: time, place, ihram, imam, congregation
C) Two: ihram and place
D) Four: time, place, imam, congregation

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of combining Zuhr and Asr at 'Arafat hinges on five conditions per Abu Hanifa, but the Sahibayn relax the requirement of imam and congregation, leading to practical differences in how pilgrims schedule their prayers.

Combining Prayers at Arafah: The Munfarid and the Imam al-Akbar
Intra-Hanafi dispute on combining Zuhr and Asr for the munfarid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of Abu Hanifa on combining Zuhr and Asr for the one praying alone at Arafah and explain the proofs of both Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
The one praying alone at Arafah must pray each prayer in its time – only the Hajj congregation behind the Imam al-Akbar may combine.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi disagreement on combining Zuhr and Asr at Arafah. Abu Hanifa restricts the combination to those praying behind the Imam al-Akbar, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani extend it to the one praying alone. Understanding the proof and counter-proof is essential for grasping how Hanafi jurists derive rulings from the Quran and consider practical needs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and the two positions
State the contested ruling: whether the munfarid (one praying alone) may combine Zuhr and Asr at Arafah. Note Abu Hanifa's position (no) and the Sahibayn's position (yes).
The munfarid is anyone not praying behind the Imam al-Akbar.
2
Analyze Abu Hanifa's proof
Examine the Quranic verse 4:103 cited by Abu Hanifa. Understand how 'kitaban mawquta' implies fixed times, and that the only exception is the congregational combination behind the Imam al-Akbar.
The verse establishes the principle that prayer times are immutable unless Shari'ah specifically grants an exemption.
3
Analyze the Sahibayn's proof
Understand their argument: combining is permitted to preserve the continuity of the standing at Arafah. Since the munfarid also stands, he needs this continuity.
They assume the 'illa (effective cause) of the concession is the need for uninterrupted wuquf.
4
Examine the Hanafi response (qulna)
The text refutes the Sahibayn by stating that the real reason for combining is to preserve the congregation, not the standing. Moreover, prayer and standing are compatible; a praying person is still standing.
This shows the Hanafi method of ta'lil (identification of the 'illa) and the importance of distinguishing the actual rationale from a perceived one.
5
Determine the practical consequence and relied-upon position
The thamarah al-khilaf: a munfarid who combines according to Abu Hanifa commits an invalid act (the combination is not accepted), while according to the Sahibayn it is valid. The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view.
This illustrates that intra-madhhab ikhtilaf has real implications for daily practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج
ومَن صلى الظهر في رَحْله وَحْدَه : صلى كل واحدة منهما في وقتها عند أبي حنيفة .
وفي الرواية الثانية : إذا كان محرماً قبل العصر: أجزأه، وهو قول أبي يوسف ومحمد؛ لأن الظهر لا يقف فعلها في وقتها على شرط الإحرام، وإنما يحتاج إلى ذلك لتقديم العصر على وقتها.
فإن صلى الظهر وحده، ثم صلى العصر مع الإمام: لم يُجزه ذلك عند أبي حنيفة؛ لأن الإمام عنده شرط في الصلاتين جميعاً. فإن أدرك مع الإمام ركعة من كل واحدة من الصلاتين، أو شيئاً من الصلاتين: جاز الجمع، إجماعاً.
ولو صلى الإمامُ بالناس في يوم غَيْم، ثم استبان أنه صلى الظهر قبل الزوال، والعصر بعد الزوال : فإنه يعيد الخطبة والصلاتين جميعاً. 
* قوله: (ومن صلى في رحله وحده: صلى كل واحدة منهما في وقتها عند أبي حنيفة؛ لأن المحافظة على الوقت فرض بالنص. قال الله تعالى: ﴿ إِنَّ الصَّلَوَةَ كَانَتْ عَلَى الْمُؤْمِنِينَ كِتَابًا مَّوْقُونَا ... النساء /١٠٣، أي فرضاً مؤقتاً، فلم يجز تركه إلا فيما ورد به الشرع، وهو الجمع بالجماعة مع الإمام، يعني الإمام الأكبر. فإن من صلى الظهر بجماعة، لكن لا مع الإمام الأكبر: لا يجوز له الجمع عند أبي حنيفة، كالمنفرد.)
وقال أبو يوسف ومحمد : يجمع بينهما المنفرد.
* قوله : (وقال أبو يوسف ومحمد: يجمع بينهما المنفرد). لأن جواز الجمع للحاجة إلى امتداد الوقوف، والمنفرد محتاج إليه، فإنه لو صلى كل واحدة منهما في وقتها يختل امتداد الوقوف؛ لأن المشروع أن يقع الوقوف من أوله إلى آخره متصلاً غير منقطع ؛ ليكون أفضل.
قلنا : تقديم العصر على وقته إنما هو لصيانة الجماعة، لا لأجل رعاية امتداد الوقوف؛ لأنه يعسر عليهم الاجتماع للعصر بعد ما تفرقوا في الموقف، إذ لا منافاة بين الصلاة والوقوف، فإن المصلي واقف.
Book of Hajj. And whoever prays Zuhr in his camp alone: he prays each one of them in its own time according to Abu Hanifa. In the second narration: if he was in a state of ihram before Asr, it suffices him, and that is the saying of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad; because the performance of Zuhr in its time does not depend on the condition of ihram, but that is needed only for bringing forward Asr before its time. If he prays Zuhr alone, then prays Asr with the Imam: that does not avail him according to Abu Hanifa; because the Imam is a condition for both prayers according to him. If he catches one rak'ah of each of the two prayers with the Imam, or something of the two prayers, then the combination is permissible by consensus. And if the Imam prayed with the people on a cloudy day, then it becomes evident that he prayed Zuhr before noon and Asr after noon, then he repeats the khutbah and both prayers entirely. * His saying: (And whoever prays in his camp alone: he prays each one of them in its own time according to Abu Hanifa; because preserving the time is an obligation by textual proof. Allah Almighty said: 'Indeed, prayer has been upon the believers a timed ordinance' — i.e., a timed obligation, so it is not permissible to leave it except where the Law has permitted, which is the combination in congregation with the Imam, meaning the Great Imam. For whoever prays Zuhr in congregation, but not with the Great Imam, he may not combine according to Abu Hanifa, like the one praying alone.) And Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: the one praying alone combines them. * His saying: (And Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: the one praying alone combines them) because the permissibility of combination is due to the need for extending the standing, and the one praying alone is in need of it; for if he prays each of them in its own time, the extension of standing would be disrupted, because what is prescribed is that the standing occurs from its beginning to its end continuously, uninterruptedly, to be more excellent. We said: bringing forward Asr before its time is only to preserve the congregation, not for the sake of maintaining the extension of standing; because it would be difficult for them to gather for Asr after they have dispersed at the standing place, since there is no contradiction between prayer and standing, for the person praying is standing.
Source pages p. 355

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the combining of Zuhr and Asr prayers at Arafah during Hajj. The issue is whether this combination is restricted to those praying behind the Imam al-Akbar (the leader of the Hajj) or whether it is also permissible for one who prays alone (al-munfarid) or behind a local imam. The passage begins by stating the ruling of Abu Hanifa: if someone prays Zuhr alone in his camp, he must pray each prayer in its own time—meaning he does not combine. However, in a second narration attributed to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (al-Shaybani), if a person is in ihram before the time of Asr, combining is permissible for him because Zuhr's validity does not depend on the condition of ihram; the only reason for combining is to allow Asr to be offered early. The text then addresses a scenario: if a person prays Zuhr alone and then catches Asr with the Imam, Abu Hanifa says this does not make the combination valid because the Imam is a condition for both prayers. If the person catches even one rak'ah of each with the Imam, the combination is valid by consensus. The commentary expands on Abu Hanifa's proof, citing the Quranic verse that prayer is a timed obligation (kitabun mawquta). This means the obligation is tied to specific times, and cannot be abandoned except where Shari'ah has allowed, and the only allowance is for the congregation behind the Imam al-Akbar. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue that the one praying alone can also combine because the purpose of combining is to prevent interruption of the standing at Arafah, which should be continuous. The one praying alone also needs this continuity. The Hanafi response (qulna) refutes this by stating that the reason for combining is to preserve the congregation, not continuity of standing. There is no contradiction between prayer and standing, as a praying person is still standing. Therefore, the need for continuity does not justify combining for the one who is alone.

Key Terms
الجمع (al-jam'): Combining two prayers (Zuhr and Asr) at Arafah by bringing Asr forward to the time of Zuhr.
المنفرد (al-munfarid): The person who prays Zuhr alone in his camp, not in the congregation behind the Imam al-Akbar.
الإمام الأكبر (al-imam al-akbar): The leader of the Hajj (usually the caliph or his appointed official) who leads the combined prayer at Arafah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) When praying behind any imam (local)
C) When praying behind the Imam al-Akbar
D) Always permissible

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, combining Zuhr and Asr at Arafah is a concession limited to the congregation behind the Imam al-Akbar; the one praying alone must pray each prayer in its time.

Recommended Actions After Prayer at Arafah
Instructions on post-prayer etiquette at Arafah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the recommended actions (mustahabbat) after the combined Zuhr and Asr prayers at Arafah during Hajj and explain the specific recommendation for the Imam.

Core Idea
Stand where you wish, but face the Kaaba and engage in dhikr until sunset.

Having completed the combined prayers, the pilgrim's next duty is to proceed to the standing place (mawqif) at Arafah. The Hanafi school outlines a set of recommended actions (mustahabbat) to fill the time between Dhuhr and sunset. These acts transform the waiting period into worship through dhikr, supplication, and proper orientation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is proceeding to the mawqif and engaging in recommended activities. Ruling: mustahabb (sunnah ghayr muakkadah).
2
Locate the specific recommendations
List from text: saying takbir, tahlil, tasbih, sending salawat, making dua, and for the imam, facing the Kaaba.
3
Determine the hierarchy
Most actions are for all pilgrims; facing the Kaaba is specifically recommended for the Imam.
4
Note the historical significance
Jabal al-Rahmah is the site where Adam stood; it is to the right of the mawqif.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
* قوله : (ثم يتوجه إلى الموقف)، يعني الإمام والقومُ انصرافه من الصلاة. معه عقیب
* قوله : ( فيقف بقُرْب الجبل)، وهو يسمى: جبل الرحمة، وهو عن يمين الموقف، وعليه وقف آدم عليه السلام.
والمعنى: أنهم إذا فرغوا من الصلاتين: انتشروا، ووقف كل واحد منهم حيث شاء، ويكبرون ويهللون ويسبحون بخشوع وتذلل، ويصلون على النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام ويدعون بحوائجهم إلى غروب الشمس.
ويستحب أن يقف الإمام متوجهاً إلى الكعبة.
* His saying: (Then he proceeds to the standing place), meaning the Imam and the people after their departure from prayer. With him after? * His saying: (And he stands near the mountain), and it is called the Mountain of Mercy, and it is to the right of the standing place, and Adam (peace be upon him) stood upon it. And the meaning: that when they finish the two prayers, they disperse, and each one stands wherever he wishes, and they say takbir, tahlil, and tasbih with humility and submission, and they send blessings upon the Prophet (peace and blessings be upon him) and they supplicate for their needs until sunset. And it is recommended that the Imam stands facing the Kaaba.
Source pages p. 356

Commentary
This passage provides rulings and recommendations regarding the actions after the combined Zuhr and Asr prayers at Arafah. The commentator explains the matn's phrase 'then he proceeds to the standing place' (al-mawqif), meaning the Imam and the congregation after they finish the prayers. The standing place is near the Mountain of Mercy (Jabal al-Rahmah), which lies to the right of the mawqif and is historically where Prophet Adam (AS) stood. After the prayers, the pilgrims disperse and each stands freely wherever they wish within Arafah. They are to engage in dhikr: glorifying Allah (takbir, tahlil, tasbih), sending blessings on the Prophet, and making personal supplications until sunset. It is specifically recommended (mustahabb) for the Imam to face the Kaaba while standing.

Key Terms
الموقف (al-mawqif): The specific area within Arafah where pilgrims stand during the Hajj day.
جبل الرحمة (jabal al-rahah): The Mountain of Mercy, a hill within Arafah near which it is recommended to stand.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The time at Arafah after prayer is for dhikr, dua, and facing the Kaaba—these mustahabb acts complete the wuquf.

All of Arafah is a Standing Place Except Batin Urana
A concise legal ruling defining the spatial boundaries of wuquf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the boundaries of the standing place at Arafah and identify the specific excluded area that invalidates the wuquf.

Core Idea
The entire plain of Arafah is valid for wuquf except the valley of Batin Urana – standing there invalidates the Hajj.

This lesson clarifies a critical spatial ruling in Hajj: where exactly must the pilgrim stand for the essential ritual of wuquf at Arafah? The matn concisely states the rule: all of Arafah is valid except Batin Urana. We will explore the practical implications and consequences of this exception.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal status
The act is the standing (wuquf) at Arafah on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah. In the Hanafi school, wuquf is a pillar (fard) of Hajj; its validity depends on fulfilling certain conditions.
2
Locate the exception in the ruling
The text explicitly states 'all of Arafah is a standing place except the valley of Urana (Batin Urana).' Recognize that Batin Urana is excluded, so standing there does not count as wuquf.
Batin Urana is a well-known valley within the greater Arafah area.
3
Understand the consequence of the exception
If a pilgrim stands in Batin Urana, the wuquf is invalid (batil), rendering the entire Hajj invalid. The pilgrim must repeat the Hajj in a future year.
There is no compensation (dam) for this; the act itself is void.
4
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Given a modern pilgrim with GPS maps, ensure they know where the boundaries lie. The ruling is absolute: intention does not override the physical location.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وعرفات كلُّها موقف إلا بطنَ عُرَنَةَ).
His saying: (And all of Arafat is a standing place except the valley of Urana).
Source pages p. 356

Commentary
This brief passage is a direct ruling from the matn, commented upon by the author. It states that the entire area of Arafah is a valid place for the Wuquf (standing) of Hajj, with one specific exception: Batin Urana (the valley of Urana). This means that if a pilgrim stands in Batin Urana, his Wuquf is not valid, and he must be within the boundaries of Arafah proper. The commentator does not elaborate further here, but this is a well-known ruling in the Hanafi school: Batin Urana is excluded from Arafah and therefore not acceptable for the essential ritual of standing.

Key Terms
عرفة (Arafah): The plain near Mecca where the Hajj standing ritual takes place on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah.
بطن عرنة (Batin Urana): A valley within the greater Arafah area that is excluded from the standing place.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The Mountain of Mercy
B) Batin Urana
C) The entire plain
D) Near the mosque of Namirah

Key Takeaway
The standing (wuquf) at Arafah is only valid if performed within the boundaries of Arafah proper, excluding the valley of Batin Urana.

Combining Prayers at Arafat for the Individual Pilgrim
Intra-Hanafi dispute on combining for the munfarid at Arafat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on combining prayers for the individual pilgrim at Arafat and state the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
The individual pilgrim does not combine Zuhr and Asr because the concession is for congregation, not continuity of standing.

When performing Hajj, the congregation at Arafat combines Zuhr and Asr. But what about a pilgrim praying alone? This passage presents an intra-Hanafi debate: the Sahibayn argue combining helps maintain continuous standing, while the relied-upon view counters that the concession is only to preserve the congregation. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to identify the effective cause (illah) behind a ruling.

Guided Path
1
State the issue and the two positions
Identify exactly what is disputed: whether the individual (munfarid) combines Zuhr and Asr at Arafat. Note that Abu Hanifa says no, the Sahibayn say yes.
Remember that the Sahibayn are Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
2
Follow the Sahibayn's proof
The Sahibayn argue that the reason for combining is the need for uninterrupted standing (wuquf). Since the individual also benefits from continuous standing, he should combine.
They use qiyas: the congregation's illah extends to the individual.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The text (قلنا) refutes this by stating that the actual reason for combining is preservation of the congregation (صيانة الجماعة), not standing continuity. Prayer and standing are not mutually exclusive.
This is a classic case of tanqih al-manat: refining the correct illah.
4
Determine the thamarah and tarjih
The practical consequence: the individual either combines or does not. The mufta bihi is the position of Abu Hanifa (no combining).
The tarjih is based on the correct identification of the illah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال أبو يوسف ومحمد : يجمع بينهما المنفرد. لأن جواز الجمع للحاجة إلى امتداد الوقوف، والمنفرد محتاج إليه، فإنه لو صلى كل واحدة منهما في وقتها يختل امتداد الوقوف؛ لأن المشروع أن يقع الوقوف من أوله إلى آخره متصلاً غير منقطع ؛ ليكون أفضل. قلنا : تقديم العصر على وقته إنما هو لصيانة الجماعة، لا لأجل رعاية امتداد الوقوف؛ لأنه يعسر عليهم الاجتماع للعصر بعد ما تفرقوا في الموقف، إذ لا منافاة بين الصلاة ،والوقوف، فإن المصلي واقف.
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: The individual combines both prayers (Zuhr and Asr) together [at Arafat]. Because the permissibility of combining is due to the need for continuity of the standing, and the individual needs that, for if he prays each one at its own time, the continuity of the standing would be disrupted; because the legislated way is that the standing occurs from its beginning to its end continuously without interruption, to be better. We said: The advancement of Asr from its time is only for the preservation of the congregation, not for the sake of maintaining the continuity of standing; because it would be difficult for them to gather for Asr after they have dispersed in the standing-place, since there is no conflict between prayer and standing, for the one praying is standing.
Source pages p. 356

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the individual pilgrim (munfarid) combining the Zuhr and Asr prayers at Arafat. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn) hold that the munfarid may combine, reasoning that the underlying cause for allowing combination is the need for uninterrupted continuity of the wuquf (standing). If he prayed each prayer in its proper time, he would have to interrupt his standing. The text then gives the Hanafi response (قلنا), which counters that the reason for advancing Asr is actually to preserve the congregation (jama'ah), not to maintain the standing. Since the individual has no congregation to preserve, this reasoning does not apply. Furthermore, there is no inherent contradiction between prayer and standing, as the one praying is still standing. This response suggests that the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that the munfarid does not combine, following Abu Hanifa's original view. The practical consequence: an individual pilgrim should pray Zuhr at its time and Asr at its time, not combining them.

Key Terms
المنفرد (al-munfarid): An individual who is praying alone, not in congregation.
الجمع (al-jam'): Combining two prayers (Zuhr and Asr) at the time of one of them, in this case advancing Asr to Zuhr time.
الوقوف (al-wuquf): The act of standing at Arafat, the essential pillar of Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because combining is only allowed for the congregation, not for individuals.
B) Because the individual's standing is not interrupted by prayer.
C) Because the individual is not required to have continuous standing.
D) Because the individual must pray each prayer at its appointed time.

Key Takeaway
The individual pilgrim does not combine Zuhr and Asr at Arafat per the relied-upon Hanafi position, as the concession is tied to the congregation.

Place and Practices of the Stand at Arafat
Rulings on the location and sunan of the wuquf at Arafat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the valid area for standing at Arafat and identify the recommended sunan for the Imam and pilgrims during the wuquf.

Core Idea
All of Arafat is a valid standing-place except Batin Urana; the day is for dhikr and du'a.

This passage from al-Jawhara al-Nayyira explains the rulings of the wuquf at Arafat, the essential ritual of Hajj. It clarifies the boundaries of the standing-place and details the recommended practices for the Imam and the congregation, emphasizing humility and supplication.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its category
Recognize that the wuquf is a rukn (pillar) of Hajj, and the passage focuses on its location and recommended practices (sunan).
2
Determine the condition for valid wuquf
Note that the entire plain of Arafat is a valid mawqif except the valley of 'Urana (Batin 'Urana). Standing elsewhere invalidates the wuquf.
This is a condition (shart) for validity.
3
Identify the sunan for the Imam
List the recommended actions: facing the Ka'bah, standing on a mount to be seen, teaching the rites, and raising hands in du'a like the Prophet.
The hadith cited supports raising hands.
4
Identify the sunan for the pilgrims
The pilgrims engage in takbir, tahlil, tasbih, and du'a with humility from the time of the combined prayers until sunset.
These are sunan, not obligatory.
5
Note the special virtue and conclusion
The day of Arafat is the best day of the year, and the wuquf is the essence of Hajj. The sunan end with sunset.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يتوجه إلى الموقف، يعني الإمام والقومُ انصرافه من الصلاة. معه عقیب * قوله : ( فيقف بقُرْب الجبل)، وهو يسمى: جبل الرحمة، وهو عن يمين الموقف، وعليه وقف آدم عليه السلام. والمعنى: أنهم إذا فرغوا من الصلاتين: انتشروا، ووقف كل واحد منهم حيث شاء، ويكبرون ويهللون ويسبحون بخشوع وتذلل، ويصلون على النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام ويدعون بحوائجهم إلى غروب الشمس. ويستحب أن يقف الإمام متوجهاً إلى الكعبة. قوله: (وعرفات كلُّها موقف إلا بطن عُرَنَةَ). * قوله: (وينبغي للإمام أن يقف بعرفة على راحلته)؛ لأنه يدعو ويدعو الناس بدعائه ، فإذا كان على راحلته : كان أبلغ في مشاهدتهم له. ولو وقف على قدميه : جاز، إلا أن الأول أفضل. والوقوف قائماً: أفضل من الوقوف قاعداً. * قوله: (يدعو، ويعلم الناس المناسك). ويرفع يديه نحو السماء؛ لأن النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام كان يدعو يوم عرفة ماداً يديه، كالمستطعم المسكين»(۱). فيقفون إلى الغروب، يكبرون ويهللون ويدعون ويتضرعون، ويصلون على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ويسألون الله حوائجهم، فإنه وقت مرجو فيه الإجابة. ويكثر الواقف من التهليل والاستغفار والصلاة على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم، والدعاء بقلب حاضر، فهذا اليوم أفضل أيام السنة، وهو معظم الحج ومقصوده.
Then he proceeds to the standing-place, meaning the Imam and the people after they are done with the prayer. He says: (He stands near the mountain), which is called Jabal al-Rahma, and it is to the right of the standing, and upon it Adam (peace be upon him) stood. And the meaning is that when they have finished the two prayers, they disperse and each one stands wherever he wishes, and they say Takbir, Tahlil, Tasbih with humility and subservience, and send blessings upon the Prophet (peace and blessings be upon him) and make supplications for their needs until sunset. And it is recommended that the Imam face the Ka'bah while standing. He says: (All of Arafat is a standing-place except the valley of 'Urana). He says: (It is appropriate for the Imam to stand at Arafat on his mount), because he makes du'a and the people make du'a with his du'a; so if he is on his mount, it is more effective for them to see him. And if he stands on his feet, it is permissible, but the first is better. And standing while upright is better than standing while sitting. He says: (He makes du'a and teaches the people the rites). And he raises his hands towards the sky, because the Prophet (peace and blessings be upon him) used to make du'a on the day of Arafat with his hands extended, like a poor person seeking food. So they stand until sunset, saying Takbir, Tahlil, making du'a, and supplicating humbly, and sending blessings upon the Prophet (peace be upon him) and asking Allah for their needs, for it is a time hoped for acceptance. And the one standing should increase in Tahlil, seeking forgiveness, sending blessings upon the Prophet (peace be upon him), and making du'a with a present heart, for this day is the best day of the year, and it is the essence and purpose of Hajj.
Source pages p. 356

Commentary
This passage details the rules and recommended practices (sunan) of the standing (wuquf) at Arafat. After the prayers, the Imam and congregation proceed to the standing-place. It is recommended (mustahabb) to stand near Jabal al-Rahma, where Prophet Adam stood. However, the entire area of Arafat is a valid standing-place except for Batin 'Urana (a valley at the foot of Arafat). The passage then describes the Imam's actions: he should stand on his mount to be visible, face the Ka'bah, raise his hands in du'a (citing the hadith of the Prophet extending his hands like a beggar seeking food), and teach the people the rites. The people engage in dhikr, takbir, tahlil, and supplication from after Zuhr until sunset. The emphasis is on humility, heartfelt du'a, and seeking forgiveness. The day of Arafat is described as the best day of the year and the essence of Hajj.

Key Terms
عَرَفَة (Arafa): The plain where pilgrims stand, the essential location for the Hajj standing (wuquf).
عُرَنَة (Urana): A valley at the base of Arafat where the devil stood; it is not part of the wuquf area.
جبل الرحمة (Jabal al-Rahma): Mountain of Mercy; the specific hill at Arafat where Adam stood, and where the Imam stands.
المناسك (al-manasik): The rites and rituals of Hajj and 'Umrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is obligatory (fard).
B) It is prohibited (haram).
C) It is recommended (sunnah).
D) It is disliked (makruh).

Key Takeaway
The wuquf at Arafat is valid anywhere in the plain except Batin Urana, and the day is spent in dhikr and du'a until sunset.

Imam's Standing at 'Arafah: Mount vs. Foot
Ruling on imam's standing and teaching at 'Arafah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the imam's standing at 'Arafah and explain why standing on a mount is recommended.

Core Idea
The imam's standing on a mount at 'Arafah is recommended (sunnah) to facilitate visual teaching, not obligatory.

This passage from al-Jawhara al-Nayyirah addresses the imam's actions during the pivotal moment of Hajj at 'Arafah. It expands on the matn of al-Quduri by clarifying that the imam should stand on his mount to be seen by the congregation, making his supplication and teaching more effective. While standing on foot is permissible, the preferred method is on a mount, underscoring the importance of visibility for leading the rites.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the imam's standing at 'Arafah. The text uses 'ينبغي' (it is befitting), indicating a recommendatory command (sunnah), not obligation (wajib).
The term 'yunbaghi' in Hanafi fiqh generally implies a recommended action.
2
Determine the preferred and permissible forms
The imam should stand on his mount (راحلته) for the purpose of being seen by the people. Standing on foot (قدميه) is permissible (جاز), but the first is better (الأول أفضل).
Superiority is based on achieving the goal of visibility for teaching.
3
Locate the proof for raising hands
The text cites a hadith from Musnad al-Bazzar that the Prophet ﷺ used to supplicate at 'Arafah with hands extended like a beggar. This serves as evidence (dalil) for the imam raising his hands.
The hadith is a sound (hasan) transmission, though ahad, and its dalala is zanni.
4
Understand the wisdom ('illa) behind standing on the mount
The commentary states that standing on the mount makes it easier for people to see the imam, which enhances their ability to follow his supplication and teaching.
The 'illa is not explicitly stated as such, but derived from the phrase 'أبلغ في مشاهدتهم له'.
5
Note the overall excellence of the Day of 'Arafah
The passage emphasizes that 'Arafah is the best day of the year and the core of Hajj, encouraging abundant dhikr and du'a.
This contextualizes the imam's actions within the greater spiritual significance.

Ghusl before 'Arafah: Sunnah, Not Obligatory
Ruling on ghusl before 'Arafah with proof by qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ghusl before standing at 'Arafah and explain the qiyas used to derive it.

Core Idea
Ghusl before 'Arafah is sunnah, not wajib, by analogy to Friday and 'Eid — purification enhances the gathering but does not invalidate the standing.

A common question among pilgrims is whether they must perform a full bath (ghusl) before the key Hajj rite of standing at 'Arafah. This lesson clarifies the Hanafi position: ghusl is recommended but not required. We will explore the proof by analogy (qiyas) to Friday and 'Eid gatherings and see the flexibility in the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act in question? (ghusl before 'Arafah) What is the hukm level according to the Hanafi school?
The text explicitly says 'وهذا الاغتسال سنة' (this ghusl is a sunnah).
2
Locate the proof (dalil)
What proof does the author cite? It is qiyas (analogy). Identify the original case (asl) and the new case (far').
The asl is Friday and 'Eid prayers, where ghusl is sunnah.
3
Analyze the illa (effective cause)
What is the common characteristic (illa) that justifies the analogy? The text says 'لأنه اجتماع' (because it is a gathering).
The illa is 'large gathering', which is clear (jaliyyah).
4
Note the scope of flexibility
What alternatives are permissible? Wudu suffices, and even standing without wudu or in janabah is valid. Similarly for menstruating and postpartum women.
The text states 'ولو اكتفى بالوضوء: جاز' and 'فإن وقف على غير وضوء، أو جُنُباً: جاز'.
5
Recognize cross-madhhab difference
Is this ruling agreed upon by all schools? The Hanafi position is sunnah; some other schools may consider it wajib.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf, as noted in the al-mukhtalaf fih block.

Even without any purification, or in a state of major ritual impurity (janabah), the standing is valid. Similarly, menstruating and postpartum women may stand at 'Arafah without needing purity. The emphasis is on the recommendation of ghusl, not its obligation.

Core Idea
At 'Arafah, lower your voice in du'a—the sunnah is humility, not volume.

At the climax of Hajj, the pilgrim stands at 'Arafah engaged in supplication. How should one pray? The matn instructs earnest striving in du'a, but the commentary adds a specific manner: lowering the voice. This lesson examines the ruling and its proof from the Quran.

When to Cease Talbiyah: Hanafi vs Maliki
Inter-madhhab dispute on the cutoff of talbiyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when to cease talbiyah, explain the Hanafi qiyas to takbir in prayer, and contrast it with the Maliki position.

Core Idea
Talbiyah continues until ramy of Jamrat al-'Aqabah — the state of ihram demands continuous devotion like takbir in salah.

This passage presents a classic inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi and Maliki schools regarding the termination of the talbiyah during Hajj. The Hanafi school holds that a pilgrim should recite talbiyah from the moment of ihram until the first pebble is thrown at Jamrat al-'Aqabah. Imam Malik, however, considered the talbiyah an initial response that should cease upon standing at 'Arafah. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to follow how each school derives its rulings from analogy (qiyas) and textual reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested ruling
What exactly is in dispute? The timing of cutting off talbiyah. The Hanafi school says it continues until ramy; the Maliki school says it stops at 'Arafah.
2
State the Hanafi position and its proof
Talbiyah continues until ramy. The proof is qiyas to takbir in salah: just as takbir is recited throughout prayer, talbiyah is recited throughout ihram.
The Hanafi proof is a clear analogy (qiyas jaliy) based on the shared 'illa of continuous devotion.
3
State the Maliki position and its proof
Talbiyah is cut at 'Arafah. Their proof: the verbal answer (talbiyah) is meant to be before engaging in the pillars (arkan).
The Maliki view treats talbiyah as an initial response, not a continuous accompaniment.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response rebuts the Maliki reasoning: the analogy to takbir shows that such dhikr is appropriate throughout the worship. Ihram is a state that continues until ramy, so the symbol of ihram (talbiyah) should continue.
The Hanafi school maintains that the state of ihram is analogous to the state of prayer, both requiring ongoing remembrance.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence): Hanafi pilgrims recite talbiyah during standing at 'Arafah and beyond; Maliki pilgrims stop at 'Arafah. This difference is observable in the actual practice of Hajj.
The difference is not merely theoretical; it affects the pilgrim's recitation on the most important day of Hajj.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويلبي في موقفه ذلك ساعةً بعد ساعة، ولا ينبغي أن يقطع التلبية حتى يرمي جمرة العقبة. وقال مالك) : إذا وقف بعرفة : قطع التلبية، قال: لأن الإجابة باللسان إنما هي قبل الاشتغال بالأركان. ولنا: أن التلبية في الحج : كالتكبير في الصلاة، فيأتي بها إلى آخر جزء من الإحرام، وذلك يكون عند الرمي.
He recites talbiyah in his standing place hour after hour, and it is not befitting to cut the talbiyah until he throws the Jamrat al-'Aqabah. And Malik said: When he stands at 'Arafah, he cuts the talbiyah. He said: Because the tongue's answer is only before engaging in the pillars. And for us (the Hanafis): The talbiyah in Hajj is like the takbir in prayer; he performs it until the last part of ihram, and that is at the time of throwing.
Source pages p. 358

Commentary
This passage presents the inter-madhhab dispute regarding the termination of talbiyah. The Hanafi ruling is that a pilgrim should continue reciting talbiyah until the actual throwing of the Jamrat al-'Aqabah (the large pillar) on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah. It is not recommended to cut it earlier. Imam Malik held that talbiyah should be discontinued as soon as one stands at 'Arafah, reasoning that verbal utterance of response (talbiyah) is meant for the initial commitment, not during the core rituals. The Hanafi response draws an analogy to takbir in prayer: just as takbir is repeated throughout the prayer until the final salam, talbiyah continues throughout the state of ihram until its final act (the ramy). The Hanafi proof is a qiyas (analogy) to the takbir in salah, which is performed from beginning to end of the prayer. Thus, talbiyah is not cut at 'Arafah but continues until ramy.

Key Terms
التلبية (al-talbiyah): The phrase 'Labbayk Allahumma labbayk...' recited by pilgrims in ihram as a response to Allah's call.
جمرة العقبة (Jamrat al-'Aqabah): The largest stone pillar (jamrah) located at Mina, which is stoned on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah.
مقام (maqam): Standing place; in this context, the pilgrim's standing at 'Arafah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) When entering 'Arafah.
B) When standing at 'Arafah.
C) When throwing the Jamrat al-'Aqabah.
D) When leaving Mina.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, talbiyah is like takbir in prayer: it continues throughout the state of ihram until its final act, the stoning of Jamrat al-'Aqabah.

Sunan of Standing at Arafah: Ghusl, Du'a, and Talbiyah
Expansion of sunan with a madhhab dispute on talbiyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three sunan of standing at Arafah, explain the Hanafi ruling on ghusl and du'a, and evaluate the Maliki counter-argument regarding the timing of cutting talbiyah.

Core Idea
Talbiyah in Hajj is like takbir in prayer; it continues until the final ritual act, not stopping at Arafah.

This passage details the recommended acts (sunan) for a pilgrim during the stay at Arafah: taking a bath, striving in supplication, and continuously reciting the talbiyah. The commentator expands each point, clarifying that ghusl is Sunnah (not obligatory) and that supplication should be silent, citing the Quran. A significant dispute with Imam Malik arises over when to cut the talbiyah, which the Hanafi school resolves by analogy (qiyas) to takbir in prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three sunan
Read the matn and note the three recommended actions: ghusl before standing, intense supplication, and continuous talbiyah until throwing Jamrat al-Aqabah.
2
Extract the ruling for ghusl
The commentator clarifies that ghusl is Sunnah (not wajib), and one may suffice with wudu. Standing without purification is valid, including for menstruating women.
This is based on analogy with Friday and Eid gatherings.
3
Analyze the proof for silent du'a
The Quranic verse (7:55) is cited to support lowering the voice in supplication, establishing a general principle for du'a at Arafah.
The dalil is qat'i al-thubut but zanni al-dalala, as the verse is general.
4
Understand the talbiyah dispute
State the Maliki position: cut talbiyah upon standing at Arafah because verbal response belongs before the pillars. Then state the Hanafi position: continue until throwing, using qiyas with takbir.
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf: Maliki pilgrims stop at Arafah; Hanafi continue.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The Hanafi qiyas is strong: just as takbir accompanies the entire prayer until salam, talbiyah accompanies the entire ihram until the final ritual (throwing). This is consistent with the purpose of talbiyah as a continuous declaration of presence.

It is recommended that he take a bath before standing at Arafah. And he should strive in supplication. And he should recite the talbiyah in his standing place hour after hour, and it is not appropriate to cut the talbiyah until he throws the Jamrat al-Aqabah. And our proof: Talbiyah in Hajj is like takbir in prayer, so he continues with it to the last part of ihram, and that is at the time of throwing. * His statement: 'It is recommended for him to take a bath before standing at Arafah' because it is a gathering, like Friday and the two Eids. Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the rulings (sunan) related to the standing at Arafah. It begins with the matn (base text) by al-Quduri listing three recommendations: taking a bath (ghusl) before the standing, exerting oneself in supplication (du'a), and continuously reciting the talbiyah from the time of standing until throwing the Jamrat al-Aqabah on the day of Nahr. The commentator then expands each point. For the ghusl, he notes that it is Sunnah (as stated in al-Hidayah), and if one only performs wudu, it suffices. The bath is analogous to the communal gathering of Friday and the two Eids. Even if one stands without wudu or in a state of major impurity (janabah), the standing is valid. Similarly, menstruating and post-partum women are excused from the bath; their standing suffices. For the du'a, the Sunnah is to supplicate silently, citing the Quranic verse commanding humble and hidden supplication. The most significant part is the third point on talbiyah. The matn states that talbiyah should not be cut until throwing the Jamrat al-Aqabah. Imam Malik disagreed, saying that talbiyah should be cut upon standing at Arafah, because the verbal response (talbiyah) is only needed before engaging in the physical pillars (the standing itself being a pillar). The Hanafi response (wa lana) is that talbiyah in Hajj is analogous to takbir (saying Allahu Akbar) in prayer; just as takbir is repeated throughout the prayer until the final salam, talbiyah continues throughout the state of ihram until the final part of the rituals, which is the throwing of the Jamrat al-Aqabah. Thus, the Hanafi position maintains continuity of talbiyah through the standing at Arafah.

Key Terms
التلبية (al-talbiyah): The verbal formula 'Labbayk Allahumma labbayk...' recited by the pilgrim from the moment of ihram.
الوقف بعرفة (al-wuquf bi-Arafah): The obligatory act of being present at Arafah on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah, the essential pillar (rukn) of Hajj.
الاغتسال (al-ightisal): The bath (ghusl) recommended before standing at Arafah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does the Hanafi school hold that the talbiyah should be cut?
A) Upon standing at Arafah
B) After performing tawaf al-ifada
C) Upon throwing the Jamrat al-Aqabah
D) At sunset on the day of Arafah

Key Takeaway
Talbiyah continues throughout the state of ihram until the final ritual act of throwing, as it is analogous to takbir in prayer.

Validity of Hajj When Day of Arafah is Confused
Ruling on confusion about the day of Arafah and its validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on Hajj validity when the day of Arafah is uncertain, distinguishing between cases where correction is possible and where it is too late.

Core Idea
If confusion leads you to stand on the wrong day, your Hajj may still be valid—only if you cannot correct it.

Imagine you are on Hajj and the exact date of Arafah is unclear. You stand at Arafah with everyone else, only to later discover it was the wrong day. Does your Hajj count? The Hanafi school provides a nuanced answer based on whether you can still stand on the correct day. This passage from Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah addresses exactly this scenario, citing a prophetic hadith as evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the two possibilities
The passage presents a case: the crescent of Dhul-Hijjah is confusing, so pilgrims stand at Arafah thinking it is the 9th. Later, it becomes clear that it was either the 8th (Yawm al-Tarwiyah) or the 10th (Yawm al-Nahr). Identify each outcome.
The confusion must be genuine—they acted on their best guess (ظن).
2
Derive the ruling for each outcome
For Tarwiyah: the standing does not suffice (لم يُجزهم) because they are still able to stand on the actual Day of Arafah. For Nahr: it suffices (أجزأهم) and their Hajj is complete.
The ruling hinges on the ability to correct the mistake.
3
Analyze the rationale
The key factor is whether the pilgrims can still perform the wuquf on the correct day. If yes (Tarwiyah case), the earlier standing is invalid; they must stand again on the 9th. If no (Nahr case), the earlier standing is accepted as a concession.
This is a practical application of removing hardship.
4
Examine the dalil
The commentator cites the hadith «حجُكُم يومَ تحجون» (Your Hajj is on the day you perform Hajj). This is the proof for the concession in the Nahr case.
The hadith implies that for those in genuine confusion, the day they perform Hajj is considered valid.
5
Evaluate the strength of the dalil
The hadith is considered weak by scholars like Ibn al-Mulaqqin and Ibn Hajar. Despite this, the Hanafi school relies on it, likely supported by istihsan or necessity.
The Hanafi use of a weak hadith shows their willingness to give concession in cases of widespread confusion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو التبس على الناس هلالُ ذي الحجة، فوقفوا على ظن أنه يوم عرفة، فتبين أنه يوم التروية : لم يُجزهم ؛ لأنه يمكنهم الوقوف يوم عرفة. وإن تبين أنه يوم النحر أجزأهم، وحجهم تام؛ لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: «حجُكُم يومَ تحجون».
If the crescent of Dhul-Hijjah is confusing for people, so they stand thinking it is the Day of Arafah, then it becomes clear that it is the Day of Tarwiyah: it does not suffice them because they are able to stand on the Day of Arafah. And if it becomes clear that it is the Day of Nahr (sacrifice), it suffices them, and their Hajj is complete, due to his statement, peace be upon him: 'Your Hajj is on the day you perform Hajj.'
Source pages p. 359

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof (hadith) from the commentator. The issue arises when the exact day of Arafah is uncertain due to a lack of sighting of the crescent. The ruling distinguishes two cases: If the crowd stands at Arafat on what later turns out to be the 8th of Dhul-Hijjah (Yawm al-Tarwiyah), their standing is not valid because they still have the opportunity to stand on the actual 9th. Conversely, if it turns out to be the 10th (Yawm al-Nahr, the day of sacrifice), their standing suffices, and their Hajj is valid based on the prophetic hadith that the Hajj of those who are present (due to confusion) is accepted on the day they perform it. This hadith, though cited, is considered weak by some scholars as noted in footnotes.

Key Terms
يوم التروية (Yawm al-Tarwiyah): The 8th of Dhul-Hijjah, the day before Arafah, when pilgrims prepare and move to Mina.
يوم النحر (Yawm al-Nahr): The 10th of Dhul-Hijjah, the day of sacrifice (Eid al-Adha).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If pilgrims wrongly stand at Arafat on what is actually the 8th of Dhul-Hijjah, what is the ruling?
A) Their Hajj is valid
B) It does not suffice them
C) They must repeat the standing on the 9th
D) Both B and C

Key Takeaway
When the day of Arafah is confused, the Hanafi school grants a concession if the mistake is discovered too late; otherwise, correction is required.
