Departure from Arafat to Muzdalifah After Sunset
Ruling on departure time and naming of Muzdalifah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on when to depart from Arafat to Muzdalifah and explain the significance of Muzdalifah.

Core Idea
Depart from Arafat only after sunset; Muzdalifah is the place of meeting for Adam and Hawwa.

After spending the day at Arafat standing in supplication, the pilgrim must wait until sunset before moving to Muzdalifah. This lesson clarifies the mandatory timing for this departure and provides the historical reason for the name 'Muzdalifah'. Understanding this ruling ensures the pilgrim fulfills a wajib act of Hajj correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is departing from Arafat to Muzdalifah. The ruling is that it must occur after sunset. Identify the hukm level of this requirement.
The text states 'When the sun sets, the Imam and the people proceed.' This implies that waiting until sunset is obligatory.
2
Understand the significance of Muzdalifah
Muzdalifah is also called al-Mash'ar al-Haram. The passage provides an etymology: Adam met Hawwa there. Recognize its importance as a sacred place.
This is a historical note, not a legal ruling.
3
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Consider a pilgrim who leaves Arafat before sunset. What is the consequence? The text implies it is not allowed; the Imam and people proceed together after sunset.
Leaving early may require a sacrifice (dam) as compensation for missing a wajib.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإذا غربت الشمس : أفاض الإمامُ والناسُ معه على هيئتهم، حتى يأتوا المزدلفة، فينزلوا بها. وقوله حتى يأتوا المزدلفة وهو المشعر الحرام، فينزلون بها. وسميت: المزدلفة؛ لأن آدم عليه السلام اجتمع مع حواء فيه، واز دلف إليها، أي دنا منها.
When the sun sets, the Imam and the people with him proceed in their state until they come to Muzdalifah and they stay there. His statement: 'until they come to Muzdalifah'—it is al-Mash'ar al-Haram—and they stay there. It is called Muzdalifah because Adam, peace be upon him, met Hawwa there, and he approached her, i.e., drew near her.
Source pages p. 359

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from the commentator explaining the matn of Al-Quduri. It prescribes that after sunset on the day of Arafah, the Imam and all pilgrims should move from Arafat to Muzdalifah in a calm and dignified manner. Staying at Arafat until sunset is obligatory (wajib) for the validity of Hajj. The text also provides the etymology of the name 'Muzdalifah', connecting it to the meeting of Adam and Hawwa. The term 'al-Mash'ar al-Haram' is another name for Muzdalifah, mentioned in the Quran.

Key Terms
المزدلفة (al-Muzdalifah): A place between Arafat and Mina where pilgrims stay after sunset on the 9th of Dhul-Hijjah; also called al-Mash'ar al-Haram.
المشعر الحرام (al-Mash'ar al-Haram): One of the sacred sites of Hajj; another name for Muzdalifah.
وازدلف (wazdalafa): He drew near or approached; from which the name Muzdalifah is derived.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Leaving Arafat Before Sunset: Ruling and Waiver of Dam
Ruling on leaving Arafat before sunset with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on leaving Arafat before sunset, identify the condition for waiving the dam, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute (majority vs Zufar).

Core Idea
Leaving Arafat before sunset triggers a dam; the dam is waived if one returns before sunset and departs with the Imam.

In Hajj, standing at Arafat is the essential pillar. The sunnah time for departure is after sunset. If one leaves early, a compensatory dam is required. However, if the pilgrim returns to Arafat before sunset and then proceeds with the Imam after sunset, the dam is dropped. This lesson unpacks the ruling and the scholarly disagreement within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and default ruling
Recognize that departing Arafat before sunset is prohibited (makruh tahrimi). The sunnah is to depart after sunset.
2
Determine consequence based on timing of boundary crossing
If the pilgrim crosses the boundary of Arafat (hadd Arafah) after sunset, no penalty. If crossing occurs before sunset, a dam is wajib.
The boundary crossing is the operative moment.
3
Analyze the waiver condition from the majority view
If the pilgrim returns to Arafat before sunset and then departs with the Imam after sunset, the dam is waived according to Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad.
Return must be before sunset, and departure must be with the Imam.
4
Examine Zufar's objection
Zufar argues that the dam is not waived, analogizing to crossing the miqat without ihram, where return does not remove the obligation.
The majority rejects the analogy because the violations differ.
5
Note exceptions and special cases
If the pilgrim returns after sunset, the dam is not waived by consensus. If the Imam delays departure, the people may depart before him because the sunnah time has arrived.
The Imam's delay does not justify abandoning the sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يدفع أحد قبل الغروب، فإن دفع أحد قبل الغروب: إن جاوز حد عرفة بعد الغروب: فلا شيء عليه. وإن جاوزها قبله : فعليه دم، ويسقط عنه ذلك الدم إذا عاد إلى عرفة قبل الغروب، ثم دفع منها بعد الغروب مع الإمام. وقال زفر : لا يسقط. وهذا كما قال في مجاوزة الميقات، إنه يجب عليه الدم، ولا يسقط عنه بالعود إلى الميقات. ولو عاد إلى عرفة بعد الغروب: لا يسقط عنه الدم، بالإجماع. ولو أن الإمام أبطأ بالدفع، وتبين للناس الليل: دفعوا قبله؛ لأن وقت الدفع قد حصل، فإذا تأخر الإمام: فقد ترك السنة، فلا يجوز لهم تركها.
No one should depart before sunset. If someone departs before sunset: if he passes the boundary of Arafat after sunset, nothing is upon him. And if he passes it before sunset, a dam is upon him, and that dam is waived if he returns to Arafat before sunset and then departs from it after sunset with the Imam. Zufar said: it is not waived. This is as he said regarding crossing the miqat: it obligates a dam, and it is not waived by returning to the miqat. If he returns to Arafat after sunset, the dam is not waived by consensus. And if the Imam delays the departure and the night becomes apparent to the people, they should depart before him because the time for departure has arrived. If the Imam delays, he has abandoned the sunnah, so they are not permitted to abandon it.
Source pages p. 359

Commentary
This is a ruling with an intra-Hanafi dispute. The main ruling is that departing Arafat before sunset is prohibited. If one does so, the consequence depends on when he crosses the boundary of Arafat (the 'hadd' of Arafat). If he crosses after sunset, no penalty. If he crosses before sunset, a dam (sacrifice of a sheep or equivalent) is wajib. However, if he returns to Arafat before sunset and then departs with the Imam after sunset, the dam is waived according to the majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad). Zufar disagrees, analogizing to passing the miqat without ihram, where returning does not remove the dam. The commentator supports the majority view. Finally, if the Imam delays departure unnecessarily, the people may depart before him because the sunnah time (after sunset) has arrived.

Key Terms
حد عرفة (hadd Arafah): The boundary of the plain of Arafat within which standing (wuquf) is valid.
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal (sheep or goat) required as compensation for violating a wajib of Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a pilgrim leaves Arafat before sunset and crosses the boundary after sunset, what is required?
A) Nothing
B) A dam
C) Return to Arafat
D) Expiation

Key Takeaway
Leaving Arafat before sunset incurs a dam only if the boundary is crossed before sunset; the dam is waived if the pilgrim returns before sunset and departs with the Imam after sunset.

Recommended Acts in Muzdalifah: Location, Etiquette, and Istighfar
Sunnah acts in Muzdalifah: location, road etiquette, istighfar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the three recommended acts in Muzdalifah according to the Hanafi school and identify the Quranic evidence for seeking forgiveness there.

Core Idea
In Muzdalifah, the sunnah is to stay near Quzah, avoid the road, and increase istighfar, rooted in the Quranic command at al-Mash'ar al-Haram.

This passage from al-Jawharah al-Nayirah highlights the mustahabb (recommended) actions during the stay in Muzdalifah, a key stage of Hajj. Beyond simply spending the night, the Hanafi school emphasizes specific etiquettes: choosing a location near the historical fire site on Jabal Quzah, avoiding obstruction of pathways, and dedicating time to istighfar. These acts are not obligatory but carry great reward and are derived from Quranic instruction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three recommended acts
Read the passage and list the three actions encouraged by the Hanafi school: staying near Quzah, not staying on the road, and increasing istighfar.
The text uses 'mustahab' for each act.
2
Determine the basis for each act
Istighfar is based on the Quranic verse (2:198) which commands remembrance and then seeking forgiveness. For location, the text refers to the historical fire place on Quzah, indicating prophetic practice. Avoiding the road is to prevent harm to others.
The verse is quoted directly as dalil.
3
Classify the legal status
These acts are mustahabb (sunnah), not wajib or fard. Missing them does not invalidate Hajj but reduces reward.
The Hanafi nuance: 'mustahab' is equivalent to sunnah ghayr muakkadah.
4
Locate the Quranic evidence
The verse commands 'remember Allah at al-Mash'ar al-Haram' and then 'seek forgiveness of Allah'. The link shows that istighfar is part of the remembrance.
The dalil is zanni al-dalalah because the command is general, but the Hanafis derive the recommendation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمستحب أن ينزلوا بقرب الجبل الذي عليه المِيْقَدَةُ ، يقال له : قُزَح. ويتحرر عن النزول في الطريق ؛ كي لا يضر بالمارة. ويكثر من الاستغفار في المزدلفة؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿فَإِذَا أَفَضْتُم مِنْ عَرَفَاتٍ فَاذْكُرُوا اللهَ عِندَ الْمَشْعَرِ الْحَرَامِ﴾ [البقرة: 198]، إلى أن قال: ﴿وَاسْتَغْفِرُوا اللَّهَ إِنَّ اللَّهَ غَفُورٌ رَّحِيمُ﴾.
It is recommended that they stay near the mountain upon which is the place of burning, called Quzah. And they should avoid staying on the road so as not to harm those passing by. And they should increase seeking forgiveness in Muzdalifah due to His saying: 'When you depart from Arafat, remember Allah at al-Mash'ar al-Haram' until He said: 'And seek forgiveness of Allah; indeed Allah is Forgiving and Merciful.'
Source pages p. 360

Commentary
This passage lists recommended (mustahabb) acts in Muzdalifah. First, staying near the mountain called Quzah (also known as Jabal al-Mash'ar) where the caliphs used to light a fire. The name 'Quzah' indicates its elevation. Second, not to camp in the middle of the road to avoid obstructing the passage of others. Third, to engage in much istighfar (seeking forgiveness) based on the Quranic instruction in Surah al-Baqarah, which mentions remembrance at al-Mash'ar al-Haram and then seeking forgiveness. These are sunnah acts; missing them does not invalidate Hajj but one loses reward.

Key Terms
قُزَح (Quzah): A specific hill in Muzdalifah where it is recommended to stay; it is the place where the caliphs used to light a fire.
الميقدة (al-mīqadah): The place of the fire (for lighting), referring to the spot on Quzah where fires were lit.

Key Takeaway

Recommendations at Muzdalifah and Ruling on Imam's Delay
Expansion on recommended practices at Muzdalifah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended actions at Muzdalifah and apply the ruling when the imam delays departure from Arafat.

Core Idea
When night falls, pilgrims must depart even if the imam delays; waiting would abandon the sunnah.

The passage from al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah expands on the recommendations for pilgrims at Muzdalifah. It also addresses a scenario where the imam fails to depart from Arafat on time, clarifying the obligations of the ordinary pilgrims.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended actions
List the sunnah acts mentioned: descending near the mountain of Quzah, avoiding blocking the road, and increasing istighfar.
These are sunnah, not wajib.
2
Understand the consensus on returning to Arafat
Note that if someone returns to Arafat after sunset, the blood sacrifice (dam) for combining prayers is not dropped by consensus of the three (Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn).
Consensus within the Hanafi school.
3
Apply the ruling on the imam's delay
When the night becomes apparent and the imam has not yet departed, the people must depart before him because the time for departure has arrived.
Waiting is not permissible as it would mean abandoning the sunnah.
4
Connect to the Quranic basis
The recommendation to seek forgiveness in Muzdalifah is based on Quran 2:198-199.

Commentary
This passage discusses recommended and regulatory rulings for the stay at Muzdalifah. The author states it is recommended to descend near the mountain called Quzah, where a signal-fire was lit by caliphs, and to avoid blocking the road. The phrase 'according to the three' refers to Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Imam and his two companions), indicating that if one returns to Arafat after sunset, the obligation of blood (dam) for combining prayers does not fall away, by consensus. A key point: if the imam delays departure from Arafat and night becomes apparent, the people should depart before him because the time for departure has arrived; the imam's delay is a failing in sunnah, but the pilgrims must not abandon the sunnah. The passage also derives the name Muzdalifah from the meeting of Adam and Eve and the act of drawing near. It concludes by citing the Quranic verse commanding remembrance and seeking forgiveness at the Sacred Monument.

Key Terms
الميقدة (al-mīqadah): The signal-fire kindled on the mountain at Muzdalifah; here it refers to the place where the caliphs would light a fire to guide pilgrims.
قُزَح (quzaḥ): The name of the mountain near Muzdalifah where the signal-fire is lit; it is a non-declinable proper noun derived from 'qazaha' meaning to rise.
السنة (al-sunnah): Here refers to the recommended practice of the Prophet; its abandonment is not sinful but in this context, waiting would be abandoning the sunnah, which is not permissible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What should the pilgrims do if the imam delays departure from Arafat and night becomes apparent?
A) They must wait for the imam.
B) They should depart before the imam because the time has arrived.
C) They should skip the stay at Muzdalifah.
D) They must offer a blood sacrifice (dam).

Key Takeaway
When night falls at Muzdalifah, pilgrims must depart even if the imam delays, because the time for departure has arrived and waiting would be abandoning the sunnah.
